1 of 997 DOCUMENTS



Robinson v. Crown Cork & Seal Co.


NO. 14-04-00658-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


251 S.W.3d 520; 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 3717



May 4, 2006, Judgment Rendered  
May 4, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review granted by Robinson v. Crown Cork & Seal Co., 2008 Tex. LEXIS 5 (Tex., Jan. 11, 2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by Robinson v. Crown Cork & Seal Co., 2010 Tex. LEXIS 796 (Tex., Oct. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 55th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 02-50324A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow challenged a judgment of the 55th District Court, Harris County, Texas, granting appellee corporation summary judgment in the widow's action alleging that her husband's mesothelioma and subsequent death was caused by his exposure to products containing asbestos.


OVERVIEW: While in the Navy, the decedent maintained equipment insulated with a manufacturer's asbestos products. The manufacturer was purchased by the corporation. While the widow's suit was pending, the Texas Legislature passed Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 149.001-149.006, which limited the liability of successor corporations for asbestos-related claims and was applicable retroactively. The trial court granted the corporation's motion for summary judgment because the damages it had already paid to other plaintiffs exceeded the monetary cap contained in the statute. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally retroactive under Tex. Const. art. I, § 16 because it was a valid exercise of the Legislature's police power to safeguard the public safety and welfare. It was narrowly tailored to protect the most innocent corporations hard hit by asbestos litigation but leaving the potential pool of asbestos defendants as large as possible. The statute was not an unconstitutional special law under Tex. Const. art. III, § 56 because a reasonable basis existed for Texas's classification of innocent successor corporations.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the corporation summary judgment was affirmed.


 

2 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Diaz v. State


No. 08-99-00486-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


68 S.W.3d 680; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 5183



August 3, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied December 7, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law No. 3 of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 99-3260).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public officials sought review of a decision of the County Court at Law No. 3, El Paso County (Texas), entered in a quo warranto proceeding brought by appellee State of Texas declaring that a city was not lawfully incorporated and removing appellants from their positions as city officeholders.


OVERVIEW: Appellee State of Texas obtained, in a quo warranto proceeding, a declaration that a city was not incorporated and a judgment that removed appellant public officials from office. Appellants argued that the enactment of 1891 Tex. Gen. Laws 24 (Act), which disincorporated the city of which they were elected public officials, was unconstitutional in that it was a prohibited local law which changed the charter of the city in contravention of Tex. Const. art. 3, § 56. The court affirmed, upholding the constitutionality of the Act. A law was not a prohibited local law merely because it applied only in a limited geographic area where there was a reasonable basis for the classification and where no general law applied. While art. 3, § 56 prevented the legislature from changing a charter by creative act it did not prohibit disincorporation. The stated public purpose of the Act was to disincorporate because certain provisions of the original charter were unjust to the city's residents. In light of that purpose, a geographic classification was the only practicable choice. A local law did not violate art. 3, § 56 simply because it had a greater impact on some citizens than others.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court upholding the constitutionality of an Act disincorporating a city and the judgment removing appellant public officials from office was affirmed because the legislature was not constitutionally prohibited from repealing a charter and a local law was not prohibited because it applied only in a limited geographical area where a general law was not applicable.

 

3 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Reyes v. State


No. 04-03-00005-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


119 S.W.3d 844; 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 7421



August 29, 2003, Delivered  
August 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1] PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 24, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 399th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2002-CR-4230. Honorable Juanita Vasquez-Gardner, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to the offense of rape of a child. When he was released from prison, defendant failed to register as a sex offender. The 399th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), denied defendant's motion to set aside and dismiss with prejudice the indictment. Defendant pled nolo contendere pursuant to a plea bargain and he was sentenced to two years confinement and a fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant signed a pre-release notification form stating that he had to register as a sex offender wherever he decided to reside. Defendant moved to Mexico and then moved back to San Antonio, Texas. Because defendant was residing in San Antonio and had failed to register as a sex offender with any law enforcement agency, officers from the Texas Department of Public Safety arrested defendant. The appellate court found that an offense defined in a predecessor statute of those offenses listed in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.01(5) (2003), including rape of a child, was a reportable conviction or adjudication for purposes of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 62.10 and 62.02(a) (2003). Thus, defendant's offense was reportable. Additionally, the fair notice requirement was satisfied because his pre-release notification stated that he had to register as a sex offender. Finally, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.10 did not permit arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement and sufficiently detailed the prohibited conduct. Therefore, art. 62.10 was not unconstitutionally vague, and the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to set aside the indictment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Chapman v. State


No. 11-15-00215-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 2231



March 3, 2016, Decided 
March 3, 2016, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by Ex parte Chapman, 2017 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1045 (Tex. Crim. App., Oct. 18, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 244th District Court, Ector County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. C-42,151.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021(c), even when combined with former § 33.021(d)(2) and (d)(3), regulated conduct, and the subsections did not regulate speech based upon its content, it had to be presumed that the statute was valid and that the legislature had not acted unreasonably or arbitrarily; [2]-Section 33.021(c) and former § 33.021(d) were not unconstitutionally overbroad in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment, and defendant failed to meet his burden of showing otherwise; [3]-Section 33.021(c) and former § 33.021(d)(2) and (d)(3) were not vague in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment, as defendant did not meet his burden to show that what remained of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021 was unconstitutional in all of its applications and could never be constitutionally applied to any defendant under any circumstance.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Arias v. State


No. 04-15-00753-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


503 S.W.3d 523; 2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 10087



September 14, 2016, Delivered 
September 14, 2016, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by In re Arias, 2017 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Tex. Crim. App., Jan. 11, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 216th Judicial District Court, Gillespie County, Texas. Trial Court No. 5459. Honorable N. Keith Williams, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant failed to show Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(a)(2)(C) was unconstitutional as applied to him for treating him differently than similarly situated adults because there was no fundamental liberty interest in having a consensual intimate relationship with a child, and strict scrutiny review did not apply to the equal-protection challenge; [2]-Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(a)(2)(C) was not unconstitutional on its face for failing to require the State to prove the defendant had a culpable mental state regarding the victim's age or for failing to contain a mistake-of-fact defense as to the age of the victim because there was no mens rea as to the age listed in the sexual assault statutes and there was no fundamental right to a mens rea element regarding the age of the victim.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

9 of 997 DOCUMENTS


FM Props. Operating Co. v. City of Austin


No. 98-0685


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


22 S.W.3d 868; 2000 Tex. LEXIS 61; 43 Tex. Sup. J. 835


December 9, 1998, Argued  
June 15, 2000, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order on Cause June 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEALS FROM THE 345TH DISTRICT COURT, TRAVIS COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city brought declaratory judgment action against appellant landowners who had designated zones in local extraterritorial jurisdiction. Both sides moved for summary judgment. Denying appellants' attorney fee claims, 345th District Court, Travis County (Texas), declared Tex. Water Code § 26.179 (1995) unconstitutional and permanently enjoined appellants from designating new zones or adding land to existing zones. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Texas legislature enacted Tex. Water Code (Code) § 26.179 (1995), which allowed landowners of contiguous tracts of at least 500 acres within certain municipalities' extraterritorial jurisdictions (ETJs) to designate their property as "water quality protection zones." Seeking declaration that § 26.179 was unconstitutional, appellee city sued appellant landowners who had designated zones in the local ETJ. Parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. Without specifying any grounds, trial court rendered final judgment declaring § 26.179 unconstitutional and issued permanent injunction enjoining appellants from designating new zones or adding land to existing zones. Trial court also denied appellant's attorney fee claims. Appellants sought review. Court affirmed, holding that § 26.179 was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to private landowners. As a whole, eight relevant judicial factors weighed against the constitutionality of the private delegation. Under the Texas Uniform Declaratory Judgment Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 37.009, trial court did not abuse its discretion to award attorney fees as were equitable and just.


OUTCOME: Because delegation of legislative power was unconstitutional in statute that allowed appellant private landowners to designate property as "water quality protection zones" within appellee city's extraterritorial jurisdictions, court affirmed trial court's final judgment that declared statute unconstitutional and permanently enjoined appellants from designating new zones. Trial court did not abuse discretion by denying appellants' attorney fees.

Radford v. State


No. 11-15-00108-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 2226



March 3, 2016, Decided 
March 3, 2016, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by Ex parte Radford, 2017 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1059 (Tex. Crim. App., Oct. 18, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 350th District Court, Taylor County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 10946-D.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant charged with the felony offense of online solicitation of a minor, the trial court did not err by denying his pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus because Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021(c), (f) (Supp. 2015), which prohibited the solicitation of a minor for illegal sexual acts, was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad; [2]-Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021(c) does not forbid solicitations made with no intent to result in a meeting; [3]-Although former Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021(d)(2) and (d)(3) may not have been models of clarity, a person of ordinary intelligence would have known what conduct was prohibited; [4]-Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021(c) is an even-handed statute designed for the legitimate purpose of protecting children from sexual predators and the effect of the statute on interstate commerce is only incidental.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

In re C.B.L.


No. 08-00-00116-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 8671



March 22, 2001, Decided


NOTICE: PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the 327th District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 97-01810).


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant juvenile said repeatedly to a friend that he wanted to kill a teacher and that he would stuff a pipe bomb into the tailpipe of her car because he was angry she reported him to the principal, and such a statement was not mere conversation between two friends, nor was it political hyperbole; [2]-Since Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.06(a) distinguishes a threat to do harm by an unlawful act from other kinds of speech, it is not overbroad; [3]-The statute is not vague on its face because threats to harm another by unlawful acts are not constitutionally protected under the First Amendment; [4]-The statute provides clear standard in that it prohibits a person from a narrowly defined act, for example, threatening to do harm by unlawful action, against a specific category of persons, for example, prospective witnesses; [5]-Defendant's adjudication of delinquency was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

13 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Univ. of Tex. v. Herrera


No. 08-06-00271-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


281 S.W.3d 575; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 8826



November 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 7, 2009.
Petition for review granted by Univ. of Tex. at El Paso v. Herrera, 2010 Tex. LEXIS 144 (Tex., Feb. 12, 2010)
Reversed by, Claim dismissed by Univ. of Tex. at El Paso v. Herrera, 2010 Tex. LEXIS 479 (Tex., July 2, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 3 of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 2006-2770).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When appellee university employee's employment was terminated, he brought an employment discrimination suit against appellant university complaining he was terminated in retaliation for taking leave under the self-care leave provision of the Family and Medical Leave Act. The County Court at Law No. 3 of El Paso County, Texas, denied the university's plea to the jurisdiction. The university appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the university raised several issues challenging the trial court's denial of its plea to the jurisdiction, arguing that Congress did not validly abrogate state sovereign immunity from suit under the self-care provision of the Family and Medical Leave Act (FMLA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 2601 et seq., and, therefore, the trial court erred by denying the plea to the jurisdiction. The appellate court disagreed and held that 29 U.S.C.S. § 2612(a)(1)(D) was congruent and proportional to its remedial object, and could be understood as responsive to, or designed to prevent, unconstitutional behavior. The FMLA defined public agency to include both the government of a state or political subdivision and any agency of a state or a political subdivision of a state. 29 U.S.C.S. § 203(x) (Supp. 2008); 29 U.S.C.S. § 2611(4)(A)(iii). The U.S. Congress made unmistakably clear its intention to abrogate the States' sovereign immunity. Thus, the university's sovereign immunity was validly abrogated by the enactment of the FMLA, and the trial court properly denied the university's plea to the jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

14 of 997 DOCUMENTS


In re Shaw


No. 06-06-00004-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


204 S.W.3d 9; 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 7061


June 28, 2006, Submitted  
August 11, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing overruled by In re Shaw, 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 8354 (Tex. App. Texarkana, Sept. 26, 2006)
Petition for discretionary review refused by Ex parte Shaw, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 215 (Tex. Crim. App., Feb. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 8th Judicial District Court, Hopkins County, Texas. Trial Court No. 0518176.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 8th Judicial District Court, Hopkins County (Texas), which denied defendant's pretrial motion for a writ of habeas corpus challenging the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.12, under which defendant was charged with improper relationship between educator and student.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly engaged in prohibited sexual contact with a student of the secondary school where defendant was employed. The court held that § 21.12 was not overbroad, noting that the record contained no data about what percentage of secondary school students affected by § 21.12 were adults. Thus, even if the statute could be said to infringe on fundamental First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, rights of consenting adults, it was not shown to reach a substantial amount of protected conduct. A due process claim was not cognizable on a pretrial application for habeas relief. There was no violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because the state had a legitimate interest in protecting secondary school students of any age from the pressures, emotional strain, conflicts, distractions, and other difficulties brought on by sexual conduct with their teachers. Language in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.12(c) authorizing prosecutions under more than one section for the same conduct was not a double jeopardy violation under the Fifth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. V, because the applicable test compared elements of offenses, not conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

15 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Watters v. State


No. 05-00-01934-CR, No. 05-00-01935-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 2983



April 30, 2002, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 265th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. F97-23159-TR, F97-23160-TR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to aggravated sexual assault of a child in two cases before the 265th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas). The trial court deferred adjudication of guilt and placed defendant on community supervision. Subsequently, the State moved to proceed with adjudication of guilt in both cases, alleging he violated the terms of his community supervision. The trial court adjudicated his guilt. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended no legally or constitutionally valid hearing was held in the proceeding to adjudicate his guilt, and the statute preventing him from appealing without the trial judge's express permission was unconstitutional. He complained his plea of true did not track the allegations in the State's original motion to proceed and an amended motion to proceed was not filed. No appeal could be taken from the trial court's determination to proceed with adjudication of guilt on the original charge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b) (Vernon Supp. 2002). Thus, the appellate court did not have jurisdiction to address his complaint. The appellate court concluded the statute was not unconstitutional under either the federal or state constitution, as there was a rational and legitimate State interest in curtailing appeals from hearings, where guilt was adjudicated under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b). The appellate court found that the Texas legislature rationally chose to condition the award of the benefit of having no record of conviction for a defendant who completed the term of community supervision on the relinquishment of a right to appeal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment in each case.

State v. Acosta


No. 08-04-00312-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 7170



August 31, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by State v. Acosta, 2006 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 584 (Tex. Crim. App., Mar. 22, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sergio Acosta v. Texas, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5838 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 1 of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 20030C17899).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the County Criminal Court (Texas), which dismissed a complaint against defendant for promotion of an obscene device in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (Supp. 2004-05).


OVERVIEW: Two undercover officers entered an adult bookstore where various sexual devices were on sale. The officers saw a sexual device and questioned an employee with regard to the possible uses of the device. He showed them the device and stated what the device was used for. The officers purchased the device and defendant was subsequently arrested for violating Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (Supp. 2004-05), which proscribed an individual from promoting an obscene device. The trial court dismissed the complaint on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional, but the court reversed on appeal, stating that it was appropriate for the State to act to protect the social interest or order morality and decency by restraining commercial dealing in non-communicative objects designed or marketed for use primarily for the stimulation of human genital organs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

17 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Jefferson County


No. 06-00-00045-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


37 S.W.3d 503; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 161


December 12, 2000, Submitted  
January 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellants' Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 27, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 60th Judicial District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Court No. B-161,269.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant business owner challenged the judgment of the Jefferson County District Court, Texas, granting appellee county's motion for summary judgment in appellant's action for declaratory judgment and an injunction prohibiting the enforcement of appellee's regulations for sexually oriented businesses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a nightclub owner, filed an action for declaratory judgment and an injunction prohibiting appellee from enforcing its regulations regarding sexually oriented businesses. Specifically, appellant argued that the regulation that made it a punishable offense for anyone to consume alcoholic beverages at the nightclub, Jefferson County, Tex., Regulations for Sexually Oriented Businesses in Unincorporated Area of Jefferson County § XXII(a)(17), was contrary to and preempted by the Texas Alcoholic Beverage Code. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court that even though appellant met the requirements of adequate remedy at law by defense of a criminal prosecution and irreparable injury to a vested property interest, appellant's failure to join as a party defendant the criminal district attorney for appellee, the official authorized by law to enforce the sexually-oriented business regulations, deprived the trial court of jurisdiction over the matter.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The trial court lacked jurisdiction over the action because appellant failed to join appellee's criminal district attorney, the official authorized to enforce the regulation at issue, as a party defendant.

Collins v. State


No. 11-14-00312-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


479 S.W.3d 533; 2015 Tex. App. LEXIS 11476



November 5, 2015, Decided 
November 5, 2015, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISH. SEE TEX. R. APP. P. 47.2(b).


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 244th District Court, Ector County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. C-42,244.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An indictment charging a teacher with four counts of improper relationship between educator and student in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.12(a)(3) (Supp. 2014), which incorporated Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021 (2011), was not flawed because it failed to allege that the victim was a minor, because the express language of § 21.12(a)(3) provided that the age of the student was not relevant; [2]-Because §§ 21.12(a)(3) and 33.021(b) would prohibit educators from electronically communicating with their students about valid, non-obscene topics, § 21.12(a)(3) was unconstitutionally broad insofar as it incorporated the unconstitutionally broad § 33.021(b), requiring dismissal of three counts; [3]-Because the incorporation of § 33.021(c) regulated the conduct of requesting a student to engage in illegal sexual acts, the statute was valid.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.

In re Tex. State Silica Prods. Liab. Litig.


NO. 01-15-00251-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 1965



February 25, 2016, Opinion Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Transferred by In re Silica Prods. Liab. Litig., 2017 Tex. LEXIS 120 (Tex., Jan. 25, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 333rd District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Case No. 2004-70000.
In re 3M Co., 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 2491 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., Mar. 26, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Nowhere in their motion for temporary injunction did the sandblasters identify a person or persons to be enjoined, and to the extent they sought to prohibit an act, it was the implementation of a statute by the multidistrict litigation court (MDL), as part of its role of managing the MDL docket; [2]-The sandblasters were making a legal argument, seeking a declaration that a law was unconstitutional, and a temporary injunction was not the correct vehicle to do so; [3]-On a conclusion that a statute was unconstitutional, a court did not enjoin itself from enforcing a defective law, it merely declared the law unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.


 

20 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Lawson v. State


NO. 2-08-116-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


283 S.W.3d 438; 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 767



February 5, 2009, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Lawson v. State, 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 3477 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, Apr. 2, 2009)
Petition for discretionary review refused by In re Lawson, 2009 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1079 (Tex. Crim. App., Aug. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF WICHITA COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under the gang injunction statute, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 125.065 (2005), the 89th District Court of Wichita County, Texas, enjoined 17 members of a street gang who had allegedly engaged in criminal activity, including defendant, from engaging in certain activities. Defendant subsequently pled guilty under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.021 (2003) to violating the court's order. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Based on prior case law, the court found that § 71.021, which made it an offense to violate a gang injunction under § 125.065, was not vague and overbroad. The statute also did not violate the Nondelegation Doctrine enunciated in Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. It would have been neither practical nor efficient for the Texas legislature, which met every other year for a few months, to determine the exact requirements necessary in order to prevent gang members from engaging in future gang activities. Further, the legislature merely asked the trial courts to impose reasonable requirements, while retaining the power to make the law by determining that a violation of the requirements, even those judicially imposed, was an offense. Although defendant failed to preserve his as-applied challenge base on service of process, the court noted that any failure to serve process on defendant's biological mother did not adversely affect defendant's interests because defendant's guardian or custodian received notice of the injunction hearing and appeared.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

23 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Forcey v. State


No. 10-09-00335-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 3830



May 19, 2010, Opinion Delivered 
May 19, 2010, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review granted by In re Forcey, 2010 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1277 (Tex. Crim. App., Oct. 6, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Ex parte Forcey, 2016 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 146 (Tex. Crim. App., Feb. 10, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
From the 249th District Court, Johnson County, Texas. Trial Court No. F43132.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a hearing granting a transfer to adult court, defendant juvenile was convicted in the 249th District Court, Johnson County (Texas) of capital murder and sentenced to an automatic life sentence without the possibility of parole, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.31(a) (2003). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised various issues, but the court affirmed. Given that the legislature chose not to apply the parole eligibility amendment retroactively to juveniles who have already been sentenced for a capital murder, the court found it inappropriate to judicially amend Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.31(a)(1). Until the United States Supreme Court or the Texas Court of Criminal Appeals determined otherwise, the Texas sentencing scheme mandating life without parole for a juvenile convicted of capital murder did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. Defendant sentence was not grossly disproportionate. He was convicted of shooting a store clerk in the head multiple times during a robbery. Even if the sentence was sufficient to create an inference of gross disproportionality, there was no evidence allowed the court to compare defendant's sentence to other sentences. The summons expressly referred to the attached petition and the petition contained references to criminal proceedings in criminal court. Thus, the court overruled defendant's claim that the summons was invalid under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.02(b) (2009).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

25 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Retzlaff v. GoAmerica Communs. Corp.


No. 08-09-00115-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


356 S.W.3d 689; 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 8020



October 7, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 3, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the County Court at Law Number Three of Bexar County, Texas. (TC# 338432).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner challenged a decision of the County Court at Law Number Three of Bexar County (Texas), which (1) prohibited him from (a) filing any motions or litigation unless granted permission, and (b) appearing or contacting certain persons, and later (2) dismissed with prejudice his suit against appellees, a company, its founder, and employees, for emotional distress and negligence, and (3) declared the homeowner a vexatious litigant.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner alleged that the company relayed a profane phone call to him. He sued, but the trial court dismissed the suit, declared him to be a vexatious litigant, and entered injunctive provisions and prohibitions. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The homeowner's threat of additional litigation did not justify a summary determination that he was vexatious. However, it did justify an expedited hearing, for purposes of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 11.053(a). Because he failed to attack all of the independent grounds supporting the finding that he did not have a reasonable probability of prevailing on his claims, the court had to uphold the trial court's ruling on this issue. The company was the only defendant that entered a general appearance and made a motion under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 11.051, and when the homeowner failed to post security, the company filed a motion to dismiss the case with prejudice. The statutes were very clear. Because the founder and employees did not make a motion under § 11.051, they were not entitled to a dismissal with prejudice under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 11.056.


OUTCOME: The order containing various injunctive provisions was vacated in toto. The judgment dismissing the case with prejudice was reversed in part as it pertained to anyone other than the company. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed, and the matter was remanded for disposing of the remaining defendants. Nothing cast doubt on the finding that the homeowner was a vexatious litigant or the prohibition against his filing any new litigation.

 

26 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Dryden v. Dryden


NUMBER 13-01-745-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


97 S.W.3d 863; 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 938



January 30, 2003, Delivered  
January 30, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 148th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sued appellees, wife and sheriff, in the 148th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, seeking an injunction and declaratory judgment barring seizure and sale of the husband's personal property to satisfy a child support judgment in favor of the wife. The trial court entered a take nothing judgment against the husband. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife obtained a money judgment against the husband for past-due child support. Personal property belonging to the husband was then seized by the sheriff pursuant to writs of garnishment and execution obtained by the wife. The husband sued, alleging that Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.005 violated Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 49 because it allowed seizure of personal property to satisfy a judgment for past-due child support, while other sections of the property code exempted seizure of such property for satisfaction a debt. The appellate court held that the statute was not unconstitutional. Tex. Prop. Code Ann. §§ 42.001 and 42.002 (Vernon 2000) were enacted to protect debtors from unsecured creditors. A child support obligation was not, however, a debt, but was, rather, a natural and legal duty. The legislature was, therefore, within its authority to exclude child support judgments from the categories of personal property exempt from seizure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

27 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Canal Ins. Co. v. Hopkins


NO. 12-06-00411-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


238 S.W.3d 549; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 8398



October 24, 2007, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 30, 2007.
Petition for review denied by Canal Ins. Co. v. Hopkins, 2008 Tex. LEXIS 52 (Tex., Jan. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW OF NACOGDOCHES COUNTY, TEXAS.
Canal Ins. Co. v. Hopkins, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 5201 (Tex. App. Tyler, June 29, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged a judgment entered by the County Court at Law of Nacogdoches County, Texas, against it in appellee wrecker service's lawsuit under Tex. Occ. Code Ann. § 2303.156(b) (2004) to recover towing charges incurred by the insurer's insured following an accident involving a tractor-trailer owned by the insured.


OVERVIEW: The state trooper who responded to the accident ordered that the tractor and trailer be towed from the scene. They were towed to the wrecker service's vehicle storage facility. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to find that the tow was consensual. The evidence of fair market values and costs to repair was sufficient evidence to enable a reasonable and fair minded finder of fact to find that the tractor and trailer were a total loss. The trial court did not err by concluding that § 2303.156(b) was not limited to instances where title had been transferred to the insurance company. Further, the result of the trial court's interpretation of the statute, which followed the statute's plain text, was not absurd. Under § 2303.156(b), a "total loss" occurred whenever the repair costs of a vehicle exceeded the vehicle's preincident fair market value. Section 2303.156(b) contained no language requiring that an insurance company actually abandon a vehicle. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The application of § 2303.156(b) to the insurer was not a taking within the meaning of the Takings Clause. Finally, the insurer was not denied procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Owens v. State


NO. 07-99-0010-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


19 S.W.3d 480; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 2202



April 4, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 98-458639; HONORABLE SAM MEDINA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment from the County Court at Law No. 1 of Lubbock County (Texas) convicting her of possession of a gambling device in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.06.


OVERVIEW: During an undercover investigation, an officer observed numerous video lottery machines in appellant's possession. Appellant was charged with possession of a gambling device in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.06. Appellant asserted that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4)(B) (the statute) provided a defense for appellant, arguing that the statute permitted the machines. Appellee contended the statute was unconstitutional because it allegedly conflicted with Tex. Const. art. III, § 47. The trial court agreed and overruled appellant's motion to dismiss. Subsequently, the parties announced a plea agreement and appellant pled nolo contendere. On appeal, appellant argued the trial court erred in declaring the statute unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause. Applying the presumption of validity to the legislature's statutory definition of "gambling device" and considering that the constitution did not criminalize possession of gambling devices, the court concluded the trial court erred.


OUTCOME: Court reversed judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings where the presumption of validity was applied to the legislature's statutory definition of "gambling device" and where the state constitution did not denounce or criminalize ownership or possession of gambling devices.

34 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rosseau


No. 04-10-00866-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


398 S.W.3d 769; 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 9772



December 14, 2011, Delivered 
December 14, 2011, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review granted by State v. Rosseau, 2012 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1553 (Tex. Crim. App., Nov. 21, 2012)
Affirmed by State v. Rosseau, 396 S.W.3d 550, 2013 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 706 (Tex. Crim. App., Apr. 17, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
From the 186th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2010-CR-0777. Honorable Maria Teresa Herr, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 186th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, entered a pre-trial written order granting defendant's motion to quash the portion of the indictment used to elevate each count of sexual assault from a second degree felony to a first degree felony under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(f) (2011). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(f) (2011) did not merely prescribe an increased punishment range when the additional fact of bigamous conduct was proven, but required proof of the additional fact as an element in order for the first-degree felony conviction to occur. Thus, under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.01(a)(1) (Supp. 2010), the State had the right to appeal the trial court's order quashing the § 22.011(f) portions of the indictment as the order altered the face of the indictment, changed the nature of the offense on which the State's prosecution could proceed, and effectively terminated the State's prosecution of defendant for commission of first degree felony sexual assault. In addition, defendant's motion to quash challenged the constitutionality of § 22.011(f) only as it applied to him. But, an as-applied constitutional challenge could not be resolved through a pre-trial motion to quash prior to presentment of the evidence. Finally, even if an appellate court could discern a facial challenge within defendant's motion, he had failed to rebut the presumption of constitutionality by proving Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011 operated unconstitutionally in all its applications.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Hall v. Aldine Indep. Sch. Dist.


NO. 01-01-01005-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


95 S.W.3d 485; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 8493



November 27, 2002, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [**1] PUBLISH. TEX. R. APP. P. 47.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Petition Denied April 17, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 11th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 1997-01357.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged the judgment of the 11th District Court for Harris County, Texas, awarding appellee taxing units the excess proceeds from the tax sale of her real property.


OVERVIEW: The taxing units filed a tax suit against the owner in an attempt to collect delinquent taxes, and default judgment was entered against the owner. The property was purchased during foreclosure for more than the amount owed, and the excess proceeds were awarded to the taxing units to satisfy post-judgment taxes, penalties, and interest due on the property, with the balance of the excess proceeds to be disbursed to the owner. The owner argued that the 1999 amendments to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 34.02(c) of the Property Tax Code were unconstitutional, as they allowed the trial court to reopen her tax judgment and award additional moneys to the taxing units. The appellate court ruled that the owner failed to rebut the presumption that the statute was valid and failed to establish that the 1999 amendments to the Property Tax Code were unconstitutional. Also, the tax judgment provided that the owner was required to pay any additional taxes that accrued on the property until it was sold, the property was not sold for three years, and the owner was responsible for the property taxes from 1997 through 2000, when the property was sold.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

37 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Coker v. State


NO. 12-09-00331-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 9740



December 8, 2010, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE: PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
APPEAL FROM THE 2ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF CHEROKEE COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 2nd Judicial District Court of Cherokee County, Texas, which convicted him of continuous sexual abuse of a young child.


OVERVIEW: In two issues, defendant argued that the continuous sexual abuse statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.02 (Supp. 2010), was unconstitutional. The court overruled both issues. The statute had the effect of rearranging and extending the statute of limitations for some of the component offenses. Although defendant identified a hypothetical circumstance whereby the State might delay a prosecution to disadvantage a defendant, that scenario was not present in this case, and defendant otherwise failed to show that the statute was unconstitutional because it did not have a statute of limitations. Defendant also failed to show that the statute was vague or that it was vague in all applications or as applied to him. The statute was not void for vagueness because it allowed for prosecution of events that might occur over the spread of several years. Defendant also failed to show that the statute was unconstitutional because it did not require the jury to unanimously agree on which specific acts of sexual abuse he committed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Anderson Courier Serv. v. State


NO. 03-02-00332-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


104 S.W.3d 121; 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 1906



March 6, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 27, 2003.
53.7(F) mot. for extension of time filed by, 04/09/2003
Petition for review denied by State v. Anderson Courier Serv., 2004 Tex. LEXIS 245 (Tex., Mar. 26, 2004)
Writ of mandamus denied In re State, 159 S.W.3d 203, 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 1390 (Tex. App. Austin, 2005)
Costs and fees proceeding at State v. Anderson Courier Serv., 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 10457 (Tex. App. Austin, Dec. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. GN102836, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant businesses challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.18 (Supp. 2003) in the District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District, Texas, arguing it violated their rights to commercial free speech. The trial court denied all injunctive and declaratory relief. The businesses appealed.


OVERVIEW: The businesses sold accident reports for purposes of solicitation or relied on such reports to solicit clients following an accident. The legislature passed Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.18 (Supp. 2003), which made it a misdemeanor for a person to obtain information from the Department of Public Safety of the State of Texas or any other governmental entity and to use the information for the direct solicitation of business or employment for pecuniary gain. The businesses unsuccessfully challenged the statute as violating their commercial speech rights. The appellate court initially noted if the state desired to regulate truthful, non-deceptive speech relating to a commercial transaction, it bore the burden of showing it had a substantial interest in supporting the regulation, the regulation directly and materially advanced that interest, and that the legislation was narrowly tailored to advance that interest. The appellate court held the statute was neither reasonably tailored nor proportional to the harm the state sought to prevent and imposed an unconstitutional permanent ban on individuals who sought to conduct their business by using legally obtained information.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

 

39 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. State


No. 05-99-01892-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 4998



July 27, 2000, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Appeals. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MC99-R-0047-D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the County Criminal Court of Appeals, Dallas County (Texas) for speeding, arguing multifarious constitutional error, including the statute under which he was convicted was an abuse of the State's police power and the trial court did not have jurisdiction to hear his case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for speeding, arguing multifarious constitutional issues. Appellant asserted the trial court was unconstitutionally created, the State was improperly represented by the city prosecutor, the charging instrument was void, the statute involved constituted an unlawful use of police power, there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction, and the trial court lacked jurisdiction. The court summarily dealt with appellant's first, second, third, and fifth issues stating those issues had been previously decided counter to appellant's position. The court addressed his police power argument by noting driving an automobile on Texas streets was a privilege subject to reasonable regulation under the State's police power in the interest of the welfare and safety of the public and that municipalities had the authority to regulate the use of its streets. The court affirmed, holding the speeding statute was reasonable and the trial court had jurisdiction to adjudicate the case.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, because driving on Texas streets was a privilege subject to reasonable regulation under the State's police power and those regulations were rationally related to a legitimate interest. Furthermore, the trial court had jurisdiction over misdemeanor offenses arising within the territorial limits of the city that were punishable by fine.

 

40 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Rylander v. Palais Royal


NO. 03-01-00224-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


81 S.W.3d 909; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 5428



July 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 30, 2002. Petition for Review Denied October 31, 2002.
Petition for review denied by, 10/31/2002
Rehearing denied by, 12/19/2002
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Palais Royal, Inc. v. Strayhorn, 538 U.S. 1013, 123 S. Ct. 1945, 155 L. Ed. 2d 850, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3497 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 98TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-03719, HONORABLE PAUL DAVIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.
Rylander v. 3 Beall Bros. 3, Inc., 2 S.W.3d 562, 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6330 (Tex. App. Austin, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation paid a franchise tax under protest and filed suit for a refund. The corporation and defendants, the Texas Comptroller of Public Accounts and the Texas Attorney General, filed motions for summary judgment. The District Court of Travis County, 98th Judicial District, Texas, granted the corporation's motion and ordered the comptroller to refund $ 480,383 in tax plus interest and statutory interest. The comptroller appealed.


OVERVIEW: The dispute arose out of the corporation's 1993 cessation of business in Texas for franchise-tax purposes due to its merger with another company. In 1991 the legislature amended the state's franchise-tax act to establish "earned surplus" as the tax base from which to calculate the major portion of a business's franchise tax. The amendments resulted in the corporation, a fiscal-year taxpayer, owing a franchise tax computed on income earned beginning in February 1990, in contrast to calendar-year taxpayers who owed the tax computed on income earned beginning in January 1991. The appeals court held the trial court erred in finding the earned-surplus amendments unconstitutional because they disproportionately impacted fiscal-year taxpayers. The appeals court found all taxpayers falling within the class were treated equally under the amendments and that the legislation was rationally related to a legitimate governmental goal. Because the corporation did not allege a net operating loss for report year 1992, the trial court erred in determining the corporation was entitled to a business-loss carryover for that year.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and a judgment was rendered that the corporation take nothing by its suit for a tax refund.

 

41 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rosseau


NO. PD-0233-12


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


396 S.W.3d 550; 2013 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 706



April 17, 2013, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPELLEE'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM THE FOURTH COURT OF APPEALS BEXAR COUNTY.
State v. Rosseau, 398 S.W.3d 769, 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 9772 (Tex. App. San Antonio, Dec. 14, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with 29 counts of sexual assault of a child and one count of indecency with a child. The Fourth Court of Appeals, Bexar County (Texas), reversed the decision of the trial court that granted defendant's motion to quash multiple portions of the indictment that were based on the bigamy provision of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(f). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the appellate court had jurisdiction to review the trial court's order granting the motion to quash because the quashed provisions were alleged in the indictment and were a portion of the indictment, and therefore Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 44.01(a)(1) could be invoked to permit the State's appeal. The appellate court erred by rejecting defendant's facial challenge to the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.011(f) because defendant's written motion, the parties arguments before the trial court, and the trial court's ruling each discussed the statutes treatment of married people as a class. However, the appellate court properly held that defendant failed to prove that § 22.011(f) was facially unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because it had at least one valid application, namely the punishment of bigamists who sexually assaulted their purported spouses. Because defendant failed to show that it was unconstitutional in every respect, § 22.011(f) was not facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

42 of 997 DOCUMENTS


In re R.M.


No. 04-01-00011-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 6497



September 26, 2001, Delivered  
September 26, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 386th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2000-JUV-02637. Honorable Laura Parker, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 386th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, convicted defendant of indecency with a child and sentenced him to two years' probation with intense supervision. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that because the trial court failed to admonish him, his plea was rendered involuntary pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.03(b)(2) (Vernon 1996) and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 26.13(a)(5) (Vernon Supp. 2001). Registration was considered remedial rather than punitive; therefore the consequences of registration were collateral. The trial court did not have an affirmative duty to admonish a defendant prior to his plea that he had to register for sexual offender registration. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.12(b)(1) (Vernon Supp. 2001) clearly stated when the duty to register ended, it was not a matter of discretion by the trial court. Mere injury to an adult sex offender's reputation alone was insufficient to implicate a liberty interest. The registration and notification statutes had a special relationship to the state's interests that the legislation sought to protect and advance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

NO. 03-99-00489-CR, NO. 03-99-00490-CR, NO. 03-99-00491-CR, NO. 03-99-00492-CR, NO. 03-99-00493-CR, NO. 03-99-00494-CR, NO. 03-99-00495-CR, NO. 03-99-00496-CR, NO. 03-99-00497-CR, NO. 03-99-00498-CR, NO. 03-99-00499-CR, NO. 03-99-00500-CR

34 S.W.3d 671; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 8015



November 30, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TOM GREEN COUNTY, 119TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. B-98-0990-S, B-98-0992-S, B-98-0997-S, B-98-0991-S, B-98-0993-S, B-98-1001-S, B-98-0994-S, B-98-0999-S, B-98-0995-S, B-98-0998-S, B-98-0996-S & B-98-1000-S, HONORABLE DICK ALCALA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded on All Causes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Tom Green County, 119th Judicial District (Texas), granting defendant vendors' motions to dismiss indictments for engaging in organized criminal activity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a)(2) by having committed certain misdemeanor gambling offenses under either Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.03, 47.04, or 47.06.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff vendors were indicted by plaintiff state for engaging in organized criminal activity under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a)(2) by having committed certain misdemeanor gambling offenses under either Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.03, 47.04, or 47.06. Defendants filed motions to dismiss, claiming that certain statutory terms Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4)(B) were unclear and ambiguous, rendering the statute void for vagueness. The trial court granted defendants' motions to dismiss, holding that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4)(B) was unconstitutionally vague. Plaintiff appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in declaring Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4)(B) unconstitutionally vague. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the trial court erred in dismissing the indictments against defendants because they failed to sustain their burden to show that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4)(B) was void for vagueness under either prong of the inquiry into the statute's unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded because the trial court erred in dismissing the indictments against defendants as they failed to sustain their burden to show that the criminal statute they were indicted under was void for vagueness.

City of San Antonio v. Summerglen Prop. Owners Ass'n


No. 04-05-00589-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


185 S.W.3d 74; 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 9741



November 23, 2005, Delivered  
November 23, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 16, 2006.
Petition for review denied by Summerglen Prop. Owners Ass'n v. City of San Antonio, 2006 Tex. LEXIS 910 (Tex., Sept. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2005-CI-02005. Honorable David A. Berchelmann, Jr., Judge Presiding.
In re City of San Antonio, 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 10804 (Tex. App. San Antonio, Oct. 12, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order of the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, which denied the city's plea to the jurisdiction and granted a temporary injunction against the city in an action by appellees, a homeowners' association and individual property owners (owners), challenging the city's proposed annexation of their property.


OVERVIEW: The owners alleged that annexation of their areas would be a direct violation of H.B. 585 (Tex. 2005). The city claimed that H.B. 585 was unconstitutional as a special law because it only applied to the northeast area of the city. The court held that the owners did not have standing to assert their claim of violations of the procedure set forth in Tex. Loc. Gov't Code ch. 43 because the claim must be brought by the State in a quo warranto proceeding. Nor did they have standing to assert the claim that the city refused to arbitrate because the arbitration request was premature in that it was made prior to commencement of negotiations. The court also held that it was necessary for the trial court to make a ruling on the constitutionality in order to conclude that the owners had standing. Based on the language, the statute was clearly a local law, and there was no evidence as to why it was reasonable to single out the areas in the statute for special treatment. Therefore, because H.B. 585 singled out a specific geographic area for special treatment, it was unconstitutional and the owners did not have standing to assert a claim under H.B. 585.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying the city's plea to the jurisdiction and vacated the order granting the temporary injunction against the city. The court dismissed appellees' claim against the city.

Ibenyenwa v. State


NO. 02-10-00142-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


367 S.W.3d 420; 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 2333



March 22, 2012, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by In re Ibenyenwa, 2012 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1023 (Tex. Crim. App., Aug. 22, 2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by, Reserved by Ex parte Ibenyenwa, 2014 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 759 (Tex. Crim. App., Aug. 20, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 3 OF TARRANT COUNTY.
Ibenyenwa v. State, 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 9908 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, Dec. 15, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District court No. 3 of Tarrant County (Texas), which convicted him of continuous sexual abuse, two convictions of aggravated sexual assault, and two convictions of indecency with a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from one conviction for continuous sexual abuse, two convictions for aggravated sexual assault, and two convictions for indecency with a child. The appellate court affirmed the conviction for continuous sexual abuse but vacated his convictions on counts two through three for aggravated sexual assault and counts four through five for indecency with a child. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting the entirety of the child's interview in response to questioning by the defense under Tex. R. Evid. 107 and 403. The State conceded that if it overruled defendant's first and third points so as to affirm his conviction on the continuous sexual abuse count, it was required to reverse the remainder of the convictions for aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child under U.S. Const. amend. V; Tex. Const. art. I, § 14; Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.02(e) (Supp. 2011). Accordingly, the appellate court sustained defendant's second point and vacated those four convictions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction for continuous sexual abuse and vacated his convictions for aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child.

Affirmed by, affirmed on other grounds by, in part Ex parte Ellis, 309 S.W.3d 71, 2010 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 479 (Tex. Crim. App., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. D-1-DC-2005-904122, 9040564, 9040570, 9040571, 9040572, 9040573, 9040574, 9040575, 9040576, 9040577, 9040565, 9040566, 9040567, 9040568, 9040569, 9040598 & D1DC-05-904121. HONORABLE BOB PERKINS, JUDGE PRESIDING.
Ex parte Ellis, 275 S.W.3d 74, 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 6472 (Tex. App. Austin, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two accused persons, challenged a decision from the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District, Texas, which denied their habeas corpus petitions. Specifically, the petitions sought the dismissal of indictments accusing them of accepting unlawful campaign contributions and money laundering.


OVERVIEW: The indictments alleged violations of Tex. Elec. Code Ann. §§ 253.003, 253.094 (2003), as well as violations of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 34.02 (Supp. 2008). A petition of habeas corpus was filed seeking the dismissal of the indictments based on overbreadth and vagueness. After the petition was denied, this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the Texas Election Code's prohibitions on the making and accepting of corporate political contributions were not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The challenged statutes gave constitutionally adequate notice of the conduct prohibited and sufficiently determinate guidelines for law enforcement. Further, there was no basis in the current jurisprudence to apply an express advocacy limiting construction to the corporate contribution restrictions in the Texas Election Code. Moreover, the pre-2005 version of the money laundering statute was not unconstitutionally vague on its face because the term "funds" in this statute did not include checks or other negotiable instruments that were not the functional equivalent of cash.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

Ibenyenwa v. State


NO. 02-10-00142-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 9908



December 15, 2011, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at Ibenyenwa v. State, 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 2333 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, Mar. 22, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 3 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 3 of Tarrant County, Texas, convicting him of one count of continuous sexual abuse, two counts of aggravated sexual assault, and two counts of indecency with a child.


OVERVIEW: According to a forensic interviewer who interviewed the child, the child identified defendant as the perpetrator and denied that anyone else had abused her. Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion under Tex. R. Evid. 107 and 403 by admitting the entirety of the child's interview in response to questioning by the defense. The appellate court agreed with the State that the defense left the impression that the interviewer had possibly manipulated the interview by asking repetitive questions even though she was not supposed to and that she excessively repeated the child's answers. Although the defense argued that the State should just be allowed to ask follow-up questions, the jury would not have had any yardstick by which to measure the effect of the interviewer's questions and techniques on the child, which occurred before the child testified at trial, other than by seeing the actual interview. Also, defendant did not preserve his constitutionally challenges, both facially and as applied, to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.02 for appellate review. Defendant raised neither challenge in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The convictions for aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child were reversed and a judgment of acquittal was rendered on those four counts. Defendant's conviction under count one for continuous sexual abuse was affirmed.

OUTCOME: Orders dismissing the complaints in appeal case numbers 05-15-00288-CR through 05-15-00331-CR reversed and cases remanded.

Walker v. State


NO. 14-05-01168-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


222 S.W.3d 707; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 2333



March 27, 2007, Judgment Rendered  
March 27, 2007, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PUBLISH -- TEX. R. APP. P. 47.2(b).


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by In re Walker, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1260 (Tex. Crim. App., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 351st District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 1022481.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found him guilty of possessing body armor, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.041(b) (2003), and sentenced him to two years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a previously convicted felon, was charged with the felony offense of possessing body armor. He filed a motion to dismiss. The trial court denied the motion. He entered a plea of no contest to the offense and a plea of true to the allegations in the enhancement paragraph. The trial court sentenced him to two years in prison. On appeal, he claimed that § 46.041 violated his right to equal protection of the law under Tex. Const. art. I, § 3. The court, applying the rational basis test, found that the statute was rationally related to a legitimate government interest of precluding felons from possessing body armor because of their greater potential to abuse the right to possess body armor. Under the rational basis review, the court respected the determinations of the Texas Legislature. The statute did not draw distinctions that made no sense. Defendant failed to demonstrate that there was no rational relationship between the prohibition for nonviolent felons and a legitimate government purpose. He only cited to general case law explaining the rational basis test. Therefore, he did not fulfill his burden to negate every conceivable basis that might support the classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

54 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Bader v. State


NO. 03-99-00014-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


15 S.W.3d 599; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 2015



March 30, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 3 OF TRAVIS COUNTY. NO. 508348, HONORABLE DAVID F. CRAIN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment in the County Court at Law, Travis County (Texas), alleging the criminal trespass statute was unconstitutional and the evidence was insufficient to establish that he was on the property "of another" to support a conviction under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 (West Supp. 2000).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of criminal trespass under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 (West Supp. 2000), arising out of an incident on a university campus. Reviewing the evidence, the court found that appellant, who was neither a faculty member, an employee, nor a student at the university, had been given a written notice not to trespass on the campus. Rejecting appellant's arguments, the court affirmed the conviction because even though the State, as "owner" of public property, had a greater burden of proving that it had a greater right of possession to university campus than did appellant under criminal trespass statute, such statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad. The court further held that the evidence sufficiently demonstrated that the officers who enforced the statute had a greater right of possession of the university campus than did appellant.


OUTCOME: Conviction for criminal trespass was affirmed because criminal trespass statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad either as written or applied and the evidence was sufficient to show that the officers who enforced the statute had a greater right of possession of the university campus than did appellant.

Bd. of Med. Examiners for Tex. v. Nzedu


NO. 03-05-00032-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


228 S.W.3d 264; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 3419



May 4, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by Nzedu v. Tex. State Bd. of Med. Examiners, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 982 (Tex., Oct. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 98TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. GN401077, HONORABLE MARGARET A. COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered In Part; Reversed and Remanded In Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Texas Board of Medical Examiners and its director, challenged a decision of the District Court of Travis County, 98th Judicial District (Texas), which reversed its decision denying a license to appellee foreign doctor on the basis that she did not pass the U.S. Medical Licensing Exam within the permissible number of attempts allowed under the Medical Practice Act, Tex. Occ. Code Ann. §§ 151.001-165.160 (2004 & Supp. 2006).


OVERVIEW: The Board included an examination attempt by the doctor prior to the effective date of a September 1, 1993 amendment to the Act that limited the number of permissible attempts to three. The trial court reversed. The appellate issue was whether counting the pre-September 1, 1993 attempt as one of the attempts allowed pursuant to post-September 1, 1993 law was an unconstitutional retroactive application of former Tex. Occ. Code Ann. § 155.056 (2004). The state appellate court reversed, holding that it was not. The limitation on exam attempts under the version of the statute in effect when the doctor applied for a license did not govern applications made prior to September 1, 2001. The statute did not annul or affect licenses granted before that date. Therefore, it affected antecedent conduct only in that it permitted consideration of exam attempts that took place prior to its effective date. Taking into account historical data did not, by itself, make the statute unconstitutionally retroactive. Moreover, it did not violate a vested right; there could be no reasonable expectation that requirements would not change. And, further, the Board's interpretation was entitled to deference.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment of the trial court and rendered judgment in favor of the Board denying the doctor's request for declaratory relief. It remanded for a determination of what award of attorneys' fees, if any, was appropriate.

57 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Juliff Gardens, L.L.C. v. Tex. Comm'n on Envtl. Quality


NO. 03-03-00174-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


131 S.W.3d 271; 2004 Tex. App. LEXIS 2036



March 4, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. GN203008, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landfill builder brought a declaratory-judgment action in the District Court of Travis County (Texas) for a determination that Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 361.122 (Supp. 2004) was an unconstitutional local or special law. The district court granted appellee Texas Commission on Environmental Quality's motion to dismiss. In the alternative, the district court granted the Commission's summary-judgment motion. The builder appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the builder had an application to build a landfill pending before the Commission, the Texas Legislature enacted Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 361.122 (Supp. 2004). The provisions of that section mandated that the builder's application be denied. On appeal, the court found that, because the Commission had neither exclusive nor primary jurisdiction to consider the constitutionality of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 361.122, and because the builder showed a justiciable controversy existed that was sufficient to invoke the jurisdiction of the district court, the district court erred in dismissing the cause. Therefore, the district court had jurisdiction to consider the merits of the competing motions for summary judgment. As to the motions for summary judgment, because the classifications within Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 361.122 were reasonable, and because the law operated equally on all within the class, the section was not a prohibited local or special law. Therefore, summary judgment in favor of the Commission was proper.


OUTCOME: The district court's alternative grant of the Commission's motion for summary judgment and its denial of the builder's motion for summary judgment was affirmed; and the decision of the district court granting the Commission's motion to dismiss was reversed.

Edwards Aquifer Auth. v. Peavy Ranch


No. 04-05-00412-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


199 S.W.3d 312; 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 1390



February 22, 2006, Delivered  
February 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 27, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 38th Judicial District Court, Medina County, Texas. Trial Court No. 04-09-17105-CV. Honorable Mickey R. Pennington, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Edwards Aquifer Authority (EAA) determined that the application for an initial regular permit filed by appellee ranch was untimely and denied the permit on that basis. The ranch filed a petition for review. The 38th Judicial District Court for Medina County, Texas, granted summary judgment in favor of the ranch, reversing the EAA's order and remanding the cause for consideration of the merits of the ranch's permit. The EAA appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ranch did not file its declaration until December 31, 1997. The Edwards Aquifer Act became effective on the date the Texas Supreme Court dissolved an injunction, making the deadline for filing the declarations of historical use December 30, 1996. The EAA asserted that when legislation was enacted affecting a general class of persons, those persons had received all process that they were constitutionally entitled to receive via the legislative process. The ranch argued that although it was not entitled to individualized notice when the Act was adopted, it was entitled to individualized notice before the EAA could implement the permit deadline resulting in a loss of the ranch's vested property rights. The appellate court ruled that the ranch received all constitutionally required notice. The ranch was charged with knowledge of the initial March 1994 deadline through the enactment and publication of the Act. The subsequent extensions of that deadline could only work to the ranch's benefit. The ranch was not entitled to individualized notice before the deadline for filing the permit application could be applied to its property right.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.
