Rankin v. Methodist Healthcare Sys. of San Antonio, Ltd.


No. 04-07-00305-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


261 S.W.3d 93; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 1577



March 5, 2008, Delivered 
March 5, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 18, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Rankin v. Methodist Healthcare Sys. of San Antonio, Ltd., 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 7923 (Tex. App. San Antonio, June 19, 2008)
Petition for review granted by Methodist Healthcare Sys. of San Antonio, Ltd., L.L.P. v. Rankin, 2009 Tex. LEXIS 209 (Tex., Mar. 27, 2009)
Reversed by Methodist Healthcare Sys. of San Antonio, Ltd., L.L.P. v. Rankin, 2010 Tex. LEXIS 211 (Tex., 2010)
Motion for rehearing on petition for review denied by Methodist Healthcare Sys. of San Antonio v. Rankin, 2010 Tex. LEXIS 362 (Tex., May 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
From the 224th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2006-CI-16732. Honorable Andy Mireles, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a judgment of the 224th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, granting appellees, a hospital and two physicians, summary judgment on her health care liability claim on the ground that the statute of repose, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.251(b) (2005), barred the claim.


OVERVIEW: In October 2006 and January 2007, the patient sued appellees after learning that a surgical sponge had been left in her abdomen when the physicians performed a hysterectomy on her in November 1995. The patient did not learn of sponge until after July 2006, when she began experiencing abdominal pain and underwent exploratory surgery. The trial court held that the action was barred by the 10-year statute of repose of § 74.251(b). On appeal, the court held that, as applied to the patient, § 74.251(b) unreasonably restricted the patient's right to sue before she had a reasonable opportunity to discover the wrong and bring suit and therefore it was unconstitutional under the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, and reversed. The court held that Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.251(b) abrogated a well established common-law claim, and that it effectively abolished the patient's right to bring claims against appellees before there was a reasonable opportunity to discover the wrong and file suit.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting appellees summary judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

West Orange-Cove Consol. Indep. Sch. Dist. v. Alanis


NO. 03-01-00491-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


78 S.W.3d 529; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 2572



April 11, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 26, 2002.
Petition for review granted by W. Orange-Cove Consol., I.S.D. v. Alanis, 2003 Tex. LEXIS 14 (Tex., Feb. 13, 2003)
 Reversed by, Remanded by W. Orange-Cove Consol. I.S.D. v. Alanis, 2003 Tex. LEXIS 71 (Tex., May 29, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. GV100528, HONORABLE F. SCOTT MCCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiffs, a conglomerate of school districts, sued in the District Court, Travis County, 250th Judicial District (Texas), seeking that the trial court declare that the tax approved in the prior case on funding for education had become an unconstitutional state ad valorem tax. An intervenor moved for dismissal. The schools appealed the trial court's grant of the intervenor's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had not given the schools an opportunity to replead; however, it determined the alleged defect was of a type that amendment could not cure. The appellate court's review indicated the correctness of the trial court's determination that the schools either could not, or did not, seek to amend the pleadings. An allegation that the schools were forced to tax at the highest allowable rate to provide the bare, accredited education was a necessary element of a cause of action they brought in challenging the funding cap. Their pleading that they had to tax at the cap to educate their students did not refer to the state-imposed obligation to provide an accredited education, as such, they failed to state a challenge to the tax as a state tax. The enriched education that they, locally, desired to provide students was not the measure for determining if the state was imposing an educational mandate requiring them to levy a state-imposed rate of tax. Their pleadings simply failed to state a viable cause of action. Accordingly, the trial court properly dismissed the claim for failure to state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

61 of 997 DOCUMENTS


City of Santa Fe v. Boudreaux


NO. 14-06-00299-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


256 S.W.3d 819; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 4049



May 29, 2008, Judgment Rendered 
May 29, 2008, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 56th District Court, Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 05CV0226.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision from the 56th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, which entered summary judgment in favor of appellee terminated police officers in a dispute involving a collective bargaining agreement (CBA).


OVERVIEW: After terminating two police officers, the city refused to participate in the arbitration step of the grievance process under the CBA. In a subsequent action filed by the officers, summary judgment was entered in their favor. In reversing, the appellate court noted that, if legislative power was delegated to a private entity, it reviewed with the presumption that the delegation was constitutional. Thereafter, the factors in Texas Boll Weevil Eradication Foundation, Inc., were analyzed to determine if the presumption had been rebutted. Delegation was read narrowly to uphold validity if possible. Here, the citizens review committee was a private group exercising broad delegated powers. The powers were legislative in nature, even though were assigned by contract. It was noted that delegations to private entities were subject to more stringent requirements and less judicial deference than public delegations. The appellate court determined that six of the eight factors under Boll Weevil weighed heavily against a conclusion of constitutionality under Tex. Const. art. III, § 1 for an appeal to the committee, as described in a portion of the CBA.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and judgment was rendered that the provision of the CBA at issue in this case was void and unenforceable.

Martin v. State


No. 05-99-00523-CR, No. 05-99-00524-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


13 S.W.3d 133; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 846



February 4, 2000, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Appeals. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MC98-R0056-D, MC98-R0057-D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the County Criminal Court of Appeals, Dallas County (Texas), which affirmed appellant's trafffic convictions in the municipal court, alleging that the municipal court was not constitutionally created under Tex. Const. arts. III, V and the evidence was legally insufficient to support the convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury in municipal court for running a red light and making an illegal left turn. The jury assessed appellant's punishment as a $ 200 fine in each case. The Dallas County Criminal Court of Appeals affirmed appellant's convictions, and appellant appealed to the appellate court. The appellate court affirmed, holding that (1) notwithstanding the legislature's choice of the words "establish" and "create" in Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 30.00082(a) (repealed), the legislation authorizing the creation of the Irving Municipal Court was neither an unconstitutional delegation of the legislature's inherent, nondelegable authority to "establish such other courts as it may deem necessary" under Tex. Const. art. V, § 1 nor a local or special law prohibited under Tex. Const. art. III, § 56. The appellate court further appellant's other arguments, including that the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions.


OUTCOME: Traffic convictions in a municipal court were affirmed because state legislation authorizing the creation of the municipal court was constitutional, the city attorney was State's proper representative in municipal prosecution, complaints were not required to be attested to, and the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions.

 

64 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Legere v. State


No. 04-00-00565-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


82 S.W.3d 105; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 2698



April 17, 2002, Delivered  
April 17, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 290th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 1999-CR-0976. Honorable Bill M. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 290th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, after he was convicted of engaging in organized criminal activity by combining and conspiring with others to promote gambling, to keep a gambling place, and to possess a gambling device, and the trial court sentenced him to two years' imprisonment, suspended his sentence, and placed him on community supervision for two years.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's lounge, an investigator with the Texas Department of Public Safety played an "eight-liner," a modified video machine, which the state labeled a gambling device, and obtained credits, which he was able to cash out for money orders with the bartender. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in: failing to include a mistake of fact instruction in the jury charge, failing to grant a mistrial, and failing to grant his motion to suppress. He also argued that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4) was unconstitutional, because it was too vague. The appellate court held that defendant was not entitled to a mistake of fact instruction, because testimony only showed that he did not believe his conduct was illegal; the mistrial issue was waived and was not error, because the trial court gave a curative instruction regarding testimony about defendant's silence; § 47.01(4) was constitutional, as the fact that certain law enforcement personnel may have misinterpreted a statute did not necessarily render it impermissibly vague; and the motion to suppress was properly denied because probable cause existed to believe that players of the eight-liners received a benefit.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

65 of 997 DOCUMENTS



Mills v. Fletcher


No. 04-06-00345-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


229 S.W.3d 765; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 3723



May 16, 2007, Delivered  
May 16, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 24, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law No. 2, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 296698. Honorable Irene Rios, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, an allegedly injured party, brought suit against appellant, an allegedly financially responsible party, in a matter arising out of a personal injury. A jury before the County Court at Law No. 2, Bexar County, Texas, awarded the allegedly injured party medical expenses. The financially responsible party appealed.


OVERVIEW: The financially responsible party argued that the award's amount for past medical expenses should have been reduced because the medical providers accepted lesser amounts for their services, writing off the balance due. On the other hand, the allegedly injured party argued that he incurred the medical charges at the time of his doctor's visit and that any amounts later written off did not affect the charges that he incurred. Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 41.0105 (Supp. 2006) required such a reduction. The appellate court agreed with the financially responsible party's interpretation of the statute. In construing the statute, the appellate court believed that "medical or healthcare expenses incurred" referred to the "big circle" of medical or healthcare expenses incurred at the time of the initial visit with the healthcare provider, while, as applied to the facts presented in the case, "actually incurred" referred to the "smaller circle" of expenses incurred after an adjustment of the healthcare provider's bill. The allegedly injured party no longer owed money to his health care providers. Section 41.0105 prevented the allegedly injured from recovering amounts "written off."


OUTCOME: An appellate court reversed the judgment, and the matter was remanded for entry of judgment consistent with the opinion.

Karenev v. State


NO. PD-0822-08


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


281 S.W.3d 428; 2009 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 961



April 22, 2009, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Karenev v. State, 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 7533 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, Sept. 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON STATE'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM THE SECOND COURT OF APPEALS DENTON COUNTY.
Karenev v. State, 258 S.W.3d 210, 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 2407 (Tex. App. Fort Worth, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of harassment, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(7). The Second Court of Appeals Denton County, Texas, held that the statute was void and rendered a judgment of acquittal. The State petitioned for discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife sought a divorce. Defendant sent his wife various e-mail messages, which became the basis for the prosecution for harassment. Defendant claimed, for the first time on appeal, that the harassment statute was unconstitutionally vague. In its petition for discretionary review, the State claimed that (1) defendant forfeited his facial challenge to the constitutionality of the harassment statute by failing to raise it in the trial court, and (2) the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The supreme court concluded that a defendant could not raise for the first time on appeal a facial challenge to the constitutionality of a statute.


OUTCOME: The court of criminal appeals reversed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court, and the matter was remanded to that court so that it could address defendant's remaining claims.

In re Commitment of May


NO. 09-15-00513-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


500 S.W.3d 515; 2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 8058

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by In re Commitment of May, 2017 Tex. LEXIS 237 (Tex., Mar. 3, 2017)

In re Commitment of May, 2014 Tex. App. LEXIS 13273 (Tex. App. Beaumont, Dec. 11, 2014)

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Even assuming that changes in the civil commitment statute required a person committed as a sexually violent predator (SVP) to move from outpatient treatment to inpatient treatment and were more oppressive than the conditions required by the patient's original order of commitment, the statute was not punitive; [2]-The tiered supervision and treatment program implemented under the 2015 amendment to the SVP statute included the possible transition to less restrictive housing and eventually to release, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 841.0831 (Supp. 2015); [3]-The trial court abused its discretion by ordering the patient's release from civil commitment in the absence of a fact-finder's determination that his behavioral abnormality had changed as required by Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 841.102, 841.121, 841.124 (Supp. 2015).

68 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Southern Crushed Concrete, LLC v. City of Houston


NO. 14-09-00873-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


402 S.W.3d 1; 2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 9124



November 17, 2010, Opinions Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review granted by Southern Crushed Concrete, LLC v. City of Houston, 2012 Tex. LEXIS 498 (Tex., June 15, 2012)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by S. Crushed Concrete, LLC v. City of Houston, 398 S.W.3d 676, 2013 Tex. LEXIS 96 (Tex., Feb. 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 333rd District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 2008-68402.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of a summary judgment from the 333rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied the company's request for declaratory and injunctive relief to prevent appellee city from enforcing an ordinance that prohibited concrete-crushing operations in certain locations.


OVERVIEW: While the company's air quality permit application for a proposed concrete-crushing facility was pending, a school was built near the property. The Texas Commission on Environmental Quality granted the permit, but the city denied a municipal permit under Houston, Tex., Code of Ordinances §§ 21-167 to 21-170 (2007) because of the proximity to the school. The court held that the ordinance was not preempted under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 382.113(b) and Tex. Const. art. XI, § 5 because it was consistent with, and did not make unlawful any acts authorized under, the Texas Clean Air Act. The ordinance governed land use, not air pollution, and thus did not conflict with the Commission's authority under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 382.002(a), 382.011(b), 382.023(a), 382.024 to decide under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 382.065 (2010) how a concrete-crushing facility would affect air quality. Although the ordinance was enacted after the company applied for the air quality permit, Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 245.002(a)(1), (b) did not prohibit the city from considering the ordinance because the land-use exception in Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 245.004(3) applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

69 of 997 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of A.M.


No. 04-09-00069-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


312 S.W.3d 76; 2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 1250



February 24, 2010, Delivered 
February 24, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by In the Interest of A.M., 2010 Tex. LEXIS 582 (Tex., Aug. 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
From the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2008-PA-01447. Honorable Antonia Arteaga, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, maternal aunt and maternal grandmother, challenged the judgment of the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, dismissing their adoption petition based on lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The children resided with the maternal aunt for approximately two years before the Texas Department of Family and Protective Services (the Department) removed the children based upon allegations of abuse. The allegations were eventually determined to be unsubstantiated. Thereafter, the biological parental rights with regard to all three children were terminated. Over nine months after the rights of the parents were terminated, the aunt filed a petition to adopt the children, and several months later the grandmother filed a plea in intervention in suit for adoption. The trial court dismissed the suit based on lack of standing. The appellate court ruled that appellants did not have standing to bring the petition for adoption. Appellants failed to file suit within ninety-days of the termination of the parental rights. Appellants sought adoption of the children, after the ninety-day period, but failed to obtain the consent of the managing conservator, the Department, to file an original petition for adoption. Also, equity could not provide standing where none existed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

70 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Beasley v. Molett


NO. 09-01-078 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


95 S.W.3d 590; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 8967


August 22, 2002, Submitted  
December 19, 2002, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:   [**1] Publish


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 22, 2003.
Petition for review denied by, Motion dismissed by Beasley v. Molett, 2004 Tex. LEXIS 27 (Tex., Jan. 16, 2004)
Motion for rehearing on petition for review denied by Beasley v. Molett, 2004 Tex. LEXIS 305 (Tex., Apr. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 284th District Court Montgomery County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 00-06-03412-CV. Honorable Judge Putnam Reiter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offenders sought to enjoin all judicial proceeding currently being conducted under the terms of the Civil Commitment of Sexually Violent Predators Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. ch. 841, and requested that appellee multidisciplinary team member be enjoined from attending team meetings. The 284th District Court, Montgomery County, Texas, denied the requested relief. The offenders appealed.


OVERVIEW: In addition to their requested relief, the offenders also sought a judgment declaring the Act unconstitutional. On review, the appellate court held that distinguishing a class of sexually violent predators from violent criminals for the purpose of involuntary commitment did not violate equal protection rights under the U.S. Constitution. Further, the distinction between the requirements to establish dangerousness under the Act, compared to an ordinary civil commitment proceeding, was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose. Due process did not mandate notice to the person sought to be committed of those preliminary procedures that preceded the petition's filing, the beginning of adversary proceedings; nor did the failure to give notice to those subject to the Act of procedures that occurred prior to the initiation of formal adversary proceedings violate equal protection. The statutory requirement that at the biennial review the judge make a probable cause finding before the person is entitled to a hearing was not a denial of equal protection or due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ex parte Bradshaw


No. 05-16-00570-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


501 S.W.3d 665; 2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 9203



August 23, 2016, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: Publish. TEX. R. APP. P. 47


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by Ex parte Bradshaw, 2016 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1468 (Tex. Crim. App., Dec. 7, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 3, Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F14-49105-J.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-It was proper to deny defendant relief on his application for writ of habeas corpus because he failed to establish Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.07(a) (Supp. 2015) was facially unconstitutional under the First Amendment due to being substantially overbroad; [2]-Section 33.07(a) was content neutral on its face because it was the deliberate use of the name or persona of another without consent and with the proscribed intent in creating any type of web page or message that was forbidden; [3]-It served a significant governmental interest of protecting citizens from crime, fraud, defamation, and threats from online impersonation; [4]-Because § 33.07(a) promoted a substantial governmental interest, the State's interest would be achieved less effectively without the law, and the means chosen were not substantially broader than necessary, § 33.07(a) survived intermediate scrutiny.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Reynolds v. State


No. 10-10-00306-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


385 S.W.3d 93; 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 7185



August 23, 2012, Opinion Delivered 
August 23, 2012, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review granted by In re Reynolds, 2013 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 99 (Tex. Crim. App., Jan. 16, 2013)
Affirmed by Reynolds v. State, 2014 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 199 (Tex. Crim. App., Feb. 12, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
From the 220th District Court, Bosque County, Texas. Trial Court No. 09-14358-BCCR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 220th District Court, Bosque County, Texas, convicted defendant of failing to comply with sex-offender registration requirements and assessed his punishment at five years' confinement. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his obligation to register had expired by the time the registration statute was amended in 2005; therefore, the amendments did not apply to him. The appellate court found that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.001(5)(A) (Supp. 2011), art. 62.002(a) applied to defendant because he had a reportable conviction that occurred after September 1, 1970. Chapter 62 appeared to require defendant to register, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.051(a) (Supp. 2011). Defendant allegedly committed the offense of failure to comply with sex offender registration requirements in 2009; therefore, the "savings clause," Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.11, would not apply to him. After the 2005 amendments to the sex-offender registration statute, defendant had a duty to register. The evidence was sufficient to establish that defendant violated the statute by not registering. The 2005 amendments were necessary to safeguard the public safety of the citizens of the state. The retroactive effect did not render it unconstitutional. The evidence concerning the jury's refusal to find on the affirmative defense of mistake of law was legally sufficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

73 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Alobaidi v. Univ. of Tex. Health Sci. Ctr. at Houston


NO. 14-06-00303-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


243 S.W.3d 741; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 8582; 27 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 347



October 30, 2007, Judgment Rendered 
October 30, 2007, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by Alobaidi v. Univ. of Tex. Health Sci. Ctr., 2008 Tex. LEXIS 300 (Tex., Mar. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 190th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 05-39746.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a retaliatory-discharge case brought pursuant to Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 451.001-.003 (2006), appellant former employee challenged an order of the 190th District Court, Harris County, Texas, granting the plea to the jurisdiction filed by appellee former employer, a state university center.


OVERVIEW: The employee conceded that the legislature had not consented to workers' compensation anti-retaliation suits against the employer. Instead, she argued the employer waived its sovereign immunity by seeking district court review of her workers' compensation award. The court observed that, in the workers' compensation case, the employer sought judicial review of the appeals panel's decision regarding compensability of the employee's injury. The employer never asserted a claim for monetary relief. In the case at bar, the employer was the defendant and had not asserted any claim for relief against the employee. Therefore, there could be no offset and no waiver of sovereign immunity. Prohibiting the employee from using the state courts to pursue her Tex. Lab. Code Ann. ch. 451 retaliatory discharge claim against the employer did not violate the state and federal equal protection, due process, and due course of law clauses. The case did not affect a fundamental right, and declining to waive a self-insuring university system's immunity from workers' compensation anti-retaliation suits had a rational relationship to the State's legitimate interest in conserving the university's resources.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

75 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Lo v. State


NOS. 01-11-00020-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


393 S.W.3d 290; 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 8936



November 10, 2011, Opinion Issued


NOTICE: PUBLISH.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 17, 2013.
Rehearing denied by Lo v. State, 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 10884 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., Oct. 1, 2012)
Petition for discretionary review granted by Ex parte Lo, 2013 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 178 (Tex. Crim. App., Jan. 30, 2013)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Lo, 2013 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1594 (Tex. Crim. App., Oct. 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 248th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Case No. 1276551.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant challenged a decision of the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied him relief he requested in his application for a writ of habeas corpus against appellee State and refused to dismiss the criminal charge against him for the felony offense of online solicitation of a minor under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021(b).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was accused of online solicitation of a minor under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.021(b). Appellant sought habeas corpus relief, challenging the constitutionality of the statute. The trial court denied appellant relief and refused to dismiss the charges. The court affirmed on appeal. Section § 33.021(b) included a scienter requirement that applied to each element. The adult had to have the intent to arouse or gratify a sexual desire. The adult also had to intentionally communicate in a sexually explicit manner with a minor or distribute sexually explicit material to a minor. The legitimate goal of the statute exceeded any potential unlawful applications of the statute. Appellant's hypothetical scenarios did not render the statute overbroad. The court held that § 33.021(b) was not facially invalid for overbreadth. Because the statute was sufficiently clear to provide adequate notice of what conduct constitutes a criminal offense, the statute was also not facially invalid for vagueness. Given the statute's target, the statute did not violate the Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Webber v. State


NO. 2-04-396-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 10266



December 8, 2005, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 16TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the 16th District Court of Denton County, Texas, to the offense of felony theft. He also pled true to the enhancement paragraphs and the trial court assessed his punishment at 18 years' confinement. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the trial court instructed the jury, it tracked Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(c) verbatim. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion for new trial based on the allegation that the parole law instruction was confusing. He further contended that the statute was vague, confusing, and misleading to the jury, and that the jury engaged in misconduct by considering the parole law as it applied to him. The appellate court noted that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a) set out, verbatim, the words that the trial judge was to use, and that because the trial court instructed the jury according to the legislative dictate of that statute, the trial court did not commit error. The appellate court held that defendant had not shown a reasonable likelihood that the jury misapplied the concepts of parole and good conduct time to assess a higher sentence than it would have otherwise assessed. The appellate court concluded that although the jury instruction on parole law was arguably confusing, the legislature mandated its inclusion in the jury charge on punishment and the appellate court would not invade the province of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 724.011, 724.012(b)(2), were not facially unconstitutional because, while they did mandate the drawing of blood under certain circumstances, they did not require that blood be drawn without a warrant. Merrick v. State


No. 05-02-01377-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 5732



July 3, 2003, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 2. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F01-57483-1.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court No. 2, Dallas County, Texas, convicting him of aggravated sexual assault, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (2003), and sentencing him to 24 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim met at a bar. Defendant gave the victim a ride home, where she alleged defendant grabbed her by the throat and sexually assaulted her. The victim testified she was able to escape after defendant fell asleep and called police. The appellate court ruled that the evidence was factually sufficient to show that the victim did not consent to defendant's penetration of her anus. The fact that defendant remained in the apartment after the assault did not show that the victim consented to sexual intercourse with defendant, and defendant's use of lubrication to facilitate anal intercourse did not show consent. Also, the evidence was sufficient to support the finding that defendant placed the victim in fear of death or serious bodily injury. The jury could have found that a reasonable person in the victim's position would have been placed in fear of death or serious bodily injury, considering defendant grabbed the victim by the throat, threw her to the ground, and threatened to kill her. The record did not show that the victim lacked the ability to understand and remember her situation and circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stockton v. Offenbach


NO. 09-0446


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


336 S.W.3d 610; 2011 Tex. LEXIS 128; 54 Tex. Sup. J. 590


March 25, 2010, Argued 
February 25, 2011, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 27, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FIFTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
Offenbach v. Stockton, 285 S.W.3d 517, 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 1733 (Tex. App. Dallas, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a health care liability claim against the doctor, alleging malpractice during the delivery of her son. However, the doctor lost his medical license and left the state before the patient filed suit. The patient was unable to locate the doctor to effect service of process but, months later, received leave to serve via publication. Although the doctor's whereabouts remained unknown, his insurance carrier hired an attorney to defend the suit. The attorney moved to dismiss on the basis that the patient failed to serve the expert witness report within 120 days of filing suit as required by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code § 74.351(a). On review, the court held that the 120-day requirement was mandatory, but even if a due diligence exception were afforded by the statute, it would be inapplicable in the instant case because the patient had four months of inactivity in her attempts to serve the doctor. The four-month gap in service activity established a lack of diligence on the part of the patient. She was thus not excused from strict compliance with the statutory service requirement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

 

84 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Rivera v. Compton


No. 08-11-00279-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


392 S.W.3d 326; 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 10758



December 28, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 8, 2013.
Petition for review granted by Tenet Hosps., Ltd. v. Rivera, 2013 Tex. LEXIS 1040 (Tex., Dec. 13, 2013)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by Tenet Hosps. Ltd. v. Rivera, 445 S.W.3d 698, 2014 Tex. LEXIS 691 (Tex., 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from 120th Judicial District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC#2011-971).
Rivera v. Compton, 2011 Tex. Dist. LEXIS 3327 (Tex. Dist. Ct., Aug. 23, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother as next friend of her daughter challenged the judgment of the 120th Judicial District Court of El Paso County, Texas, granting the motions for summary judgment in favor of appellees, doctor and hospital.


OVERVIEW: The daughter was allegedly delivered in a serious condition and suffered severe brain damage due to lack of oxygen, and lives with permanent neurological injury and disability. The daughter was fourteen years old at the time the suit was filed. The appellate court ruled that Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.251(b) (2011) violated the open court provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13 as applied to minors injured before their eighth birthday. Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.251(b) effectively cut off a minor's cause of action before the minor was legally able to assert it, thereby requiring the minor to satisfy an impossible condition, and failed to provide an adequate substitute remedy. By putting a ten-year outer limit on the health care liability claims of minors injured before the age of eight, these minors will never be able to bring claims in their own right because the statute of repose cuts it off before they reach the age of majority. Also, since the medical liability claim belongs to the daughter, and not the mother, any lack of any due diligence on the part of the mother could not be attributed to the claims belonging to the daughter.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Luquis v. State


NO. 0283-00


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


72 S.W.3d 355; 2002 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 76



April 10, 2002, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPELLANT'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW. FROM THE NINTH COURT OF APPEALS. POLK COUNTY.

Luquis v. State, 997 S.W.2d 442, 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 6735 (Tex. App. Beaumont 1999) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the trial court's submission of the statutorily-required parole law instruction, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a), at the punishment stage of trial, after the Ninth Court of Appeals, Polk County (Texas), affirmed his conviction of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering a fellow prison inmate by repeatedly stabbing him with a steel rod or "shank." On appeal, defendant argued that because he was not eligible for release on mandatory supervision, the trial judge erred in giving the jury the instruction concerning good conduct time; informing the jury about good conduct time violated his due process rights; and defendant questioned what harm analysis, the Almanza standard or Tex. R. App. P. 44.2(a) concerning constitutional error, applied in the event the submission of the instruction was in error or unconstitutional. The proper standard for review was whether there was a reasonable likelihood that the jury applied the challenged instruction unconstitutionally. The court of criminal appeals held that the parole law charge was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant, because defendant failed to demonstrate that there was a reasonable likelihood that the jury unconstitutionally misapplied the concept of "good conduct time" to assess a higher sentence as a result of the instruction, thereby denying defendant due process or due course of law.


OUTCOME: The court of criminal appeals affirmed the judgment of the trial court and the court of appeals.

 

86 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Gribble v. Layton


NO. 14-11-00856-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


389 S.W.3d 882; 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 10079



December 6, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by Layton v. Gribble, 2013 Tex. LEXIS 384 (Tex., May 10, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 306th District Court, Galveston County. Trial Court Cause No. 09FD0426.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother, individually and in her capacity as guardian of the person and estate of her disabled adult son (born in 1972), brought an action in 2009 against appellee, the alleged biological father, seeking parentage and child support determinations. The 306th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, dismissed the suit on statute-of-limitations grounds under the 1983 version of former Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01. The mother sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held that the statute of limitations did not bar the action because the residual four-year statute of limitations, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.051, applied in the absence of a more specific limitations provision, and the running of the limitations period was continuously tolled under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.001, due to the legal disability of unsound mind. The more specific statute of limitations in the 1983 version of former Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 13.01 did not apply retroactively because the statute was tolled by disability and therefore the suit had not been barred before the effective date. It was not necessary to decide whether Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 160.606 (which was in effect when suit was filed and allowed commencement at any time) could be applied retroactively. However, the court found that two factors would have weighed in favor of retroactive application: there was no settled expectation that a statute of limitations barred the action, and there was a compelling state interest in ensuring that the natural parents of a child assume primary responsibility for the child--including a disabled adult with no presumed father.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Boyd v. Kallam


NO. 2-03-362-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


152 S.W.3d 670; 2004 Tex. App. LEXIS 10530



November 24, 2004, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Petition for review granted by Kallam v. Boyd, 2006 Tex. LEXIS 840 (Tex., Sept. 1, 2006)
Petition for review denied by Kallam v. Boyd, 232 S.W.3d 774, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 564 (Tex., 2007)
Motion for rehearing on petition for review denied by Kallam v. Boyd, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 938 (Tex., Oct. 12, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed from a partial summary judgment of the 17th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) in favor of defendant health care providers in the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: A colonoscopy revealed that the patient had stage IV colorectal cancer. The patient alleged that the providers were negligent in failing to screen her for colorectal cancer after she became 50 years old, misdiagnosing her rectal bleeding as stemming from hemorrhoids, failing to diagnose her cancer, and failing to order testing that would have revealed the cancer. The court held that the providers conclusively established their affirmative defense of limitations as to the patient's claims of negligence on four specific office visits. The patient's summary judgment evidence raised an issue of fact, however, concerning whether she had a reasonable opportunity to discover the providers' alleged wrongs or her alleged injury. The patient's hemorrhoids diagnosis made it impossible for her to learn of the providers' alleged wrongs, or her alleged injury, colon cancer. Thus, the open courts guarantee of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13 precluded application of the limitations provision of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (repealed 2003) to cut off the patient's claims as a matter of law. The patient's four-month delay in filing suit after learning of her injury was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the partial summary judgment on the patient's negligent failure to diagnose claims, misdiagnosis claims, and negligent failure to order testing claims based on four office visits. The court affirmed the partial summary judgment concerning the patient's negligent-failure-to-screen-based-on-age claims and concerning the first office visit. The court affirmed the partial summary judgment for the practice on direct negligence.

 

88 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Rivera v. State


NO. 01-10-00616-CR, NO. 01-10-00617-CR, NO. 01-10-00618-CR, NO. 01-10-00619-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


363 S.W.3d 660; 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 5133



July 7, 2011, Opinion Issued


NOTICE: PUBLISH. TEX. R. APP. P. 47.2(b).


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from County Criminal Court At Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Case Nos. 1652303 & 1652305. On Appeal from County Criminal Court At Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Case No. 1683906. On Appeal from County Criminal Court At Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Case No. 1652289.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed orders of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas, denying relief in pretrial habeas corpus proceedings in which defendants challenged the constitutionality of Houston, Tex., Code of Ordinances, No. 97-75, under which each was being prosecuted with Class A misdemeanor offenses. The ordinance regulated sexually-oriented businesses and criminalized certain conduct by persons employed by those establishments.


OVERVIEW: The court held that a culpable mental state was required to prove a violation of the ordinance; that is, offenses under the ordinance were not strict liability offenses. The ordinance was not unconstitutionally overbroad or vague. It conveyed a sufficient warning about the proscribed conduct when measured by a common understanding and practice. The ordinance's provisions regulating the conduct and permitting of entertainers were authorized under Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. ch. 243. Thus, the city properly made violations of those provisions punishable as Class A misdemeanors. The ordinance was not an unlawful expansion of the city's authority in violation of the limits set forth in the Texas Local Government Code and the doctrine of preemption, as claimed by defendants. Defendants had not carried their burden to show that the punishment range for a Class A misdemeanor was grossly disproportionate to the offense of violating the ordinance. Prosecuting violations of the ordinance as a Class A misdemeanor was justified to deter continuing violations of the ordinance that legislative bodies had determined leads to greater criminal activities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders denying habeas relief in each appeal.

 

89 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Thoyakulathu v. Brennan


No. 06-05-00070-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


192 S.W.3d 849; 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 3308


October 19, 2005, Submitted  
April 27, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 336th Judicial District Court. Fannin County, Texas. Trial Court No. 36333.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical providers sought review of a judgment from the 336th Judicial District Court, Fannin County (Texas), which denied their motion to dismiss appellee widower's medical malpractice action pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.351 for failure to serve expert reports.


OVERVIEW: On the day of the deadline, the expert reports were timely filed, but service failed by reason of a facsimile transmission problem. The trial court granted a 30-day extension pursuant to § 74.351(c). The court, in reversing, held that § 74.351(c) applied only when a timely-served report did not meet the statutory definition of an expert report because it had one or more deficiencies in its contents; § 74.351(c) did not apply to a report that was not served by the deadline. Thus, the trial court was bound by the mandatory dismissal provision of § 74.351(b). The court also rejected an assertion that § 74.351, as applied, denied the widower due process and due course of law pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. The court observed that due process did not require prior notice that the law was serious about a clearly stated consequence. Mandatory dismissal was a clearly stated consequence for failing to comply with the statutory deadline, and Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.351 did not have to provide an exception geared toward last-minute misfortune in order to provide constitutionally adequate safeguards.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the motion to dismiss and remanded for dismissal of the claims and for further proceedings regarding statutory attorney fees and costs.

Southwest Travis County Water Dist. v. City of Austin


NO. 03-97-00736-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


64 S.W.3d 25; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 70



January 6, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 10, 2000. Tex. R. App. P. 47.3(c).


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-13123, HONORABLE F. SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Southwest Travis County Water District, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas) holding unconstitutional its constitutive statute, 1995 Tex. Gen. Laws 4243, in a declaratory judgment action brought by appellee, the City of Austin.


OVERVIEW: The legislature intended 1995 Tex. Gen. Laws 4243 to operate exclusively within the extraterritorial jurisdiction of a single Texas municipality, appellee. The court held that none of the reasons suggested by appellant district amounted to a reasonable basis for singling out appellant district for special treatment. Therefore, 1995 Tex. Gen. Laws 4243 was not a general law. Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 59(e) required that each special law creating a conservation and reclamation district had to comply with the general laws then in effect relating to consent by political subdivisions of the districts. The court held that Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. §42.023 (West 1999) was applicable and required that appellee had to give its written consent to extraterritorial jurisdiction. Therefore, the court held that 1995 Tex. Gen. Laws 4243 was unconstitutional as a local law authorized by Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 59 because appellee did not consent.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the court held that the disputed law was not a general law; thus, the law required appellee's consent to the creation of appellant district within its extraterritorial jurisdiction which it would not give; therefore, the law was unconstitutional as a local law and was struck down.

Leonard v. Abbott


NO. 03-03-00443-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


171 S.W.3d 451; 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 5695



July 21, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 10, 2005.
Rehearing overruled by Leonard v. Abbott, 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 8338 (Tex. App. Austin, Aug. 17, 2005)
Related proceeding at Leonard v. Hearst Corp., 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 9809 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., Nov. 23, 2005)
Petition for review denied by Leonard v. Abbott, 2005 Tex. LEXIS 874 (Tex., Dec. 2, 2005)
Motion for rehearing on petition for review denied by Leonard v. Abbott, 2006 Tex. LEXIS 116 (Tex., Feb. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. GN300-269, HONORABLE DARLENE BYRNE, JUDGE PRESIDING.
Leonard v. Abbott, 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 8766 (Tex. App. Austin, Dec. 12, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged orders of the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), which declared him a vexatious litigant pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 11.001-11.055 (2002), and which dismissed his lawsuit against appellees, the attorney general, a county, an agency, and a city, after he failed to furnish court-ordered security.


OVERVIEW: The citizen had a long history of filing lawsuits and appeals to contest the issuance and approval of bonds in the county related to the construction of new sports arenas in that locale. In affirming, the court held that the vexatious litigant statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it sufficiently outlined a standard of conduct and because a core of prohibited activity was well defined therein. Furthermore, the statute did not implicate the citizen's constitutional right to equal protection. The citizen's own pleadings belied his claim that he could not have known he was at risk of being held to be a vexatious litigant. He acknowledged that his underlying lawsuit asserted the same request for relief that had been included in one unsuccessful lawsuit or another continuously from 1998 through 2003 and should have known that there was no reasonable probability of success. The restrictions placed on the citizen were not unreasonable when balanced with the significant costs of defending his likely frivolous lawsuits in the future. The court disagreed with the citizen's claim that appellees failed to show there was no reasonable probability that he would prevail in his suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

Cash Am. Int'l, Inc. v. Bennett


NO. 99-0041


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


35 S.W.3d 12; 2000 Tex. LEXIS 82; 43 Tex. Sup. J. 1047


November 10, 1999, Argued  
July 6, 2000, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FIRST DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pawnbroker requested review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals for the First District of Texas that reversed the trial court's dismissal of respondent's suit for conversion, negligence, and gross negligence arising from petitioner's inability to return pledged property.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was unable to return a ring pledged by respondent because the ring had been stolen. Respondent rejected petitioner's offers of a like-kind replacement or a cash settlement and sued for conversion, negligence, and gross negligence. The trial court granted petitioner's plea to the jurisdiction, which claimed that Tex. Fin. Code Ann. § 371.167(a) of the Texas Pawnshop Act (Act of May 24, 1997, ch. 1008, § 1, 1997 Tex. Gen. Laws 3091, 3554; amended by Act of May 27, 1999, ch. 1399, § 7, 1999 Tex. Gen. Laws 4724, 4726) granted the Consumer Credit Commissioner primary and exclusive jurisdiction over disputes between pledgors and pawnbrokers concerning lost goods. The court of appeals reversed, holding that the Pawnshop Act provided an alternative, not an exclusive, remedy, and the court affirmed. Respondent was not required to seek a remedy under the Pawnshop Act before filing suit, so the commissioner did not have exclusive jurisdiction. Nor did the commissioner have primary jurisdiction, as there was no reason to defer to the commissioner's expertise.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the Texas Pawnshop Act in effect when respondent's suit was filed did not require respondent to exhaust administrative remedies and did not abrogate respondent's common-law claims, nor did the Consumer Credit Commissioner have primary jurisdiction over the dispute.

Lawrence v. State


NO. 14-99-00109-CR & NO. 14-99-00111-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


41 S.W.3d 349; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 1776



March 15, 2001, Substituted Majority, Concurring, and Dissenting Opinions Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of certiorari granted, Motion granted by: Lawrence v. Texas, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8680 (U.S. Dec. 2, 2002).
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 04/17/2002
Writ of certiorari granted, Motion granted by Lawrence v. Texas, 537 U.S. 1044, 154 L. Ed. 2d 514, 123 S. Ct. 661, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8680 (2002)
Reversed by, Remanded by Lawrence v. Texas, 156 L. Ed. 2d 508, 123 S. Ct. 2472, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5013 (U.S., 2003)
On remand at, Complaint dismissed at Lawrence v. State, 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 9191 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., Oct. 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 10. Trial Court Cause Nos. 98-48530 and 98-48531. Harris County, Texas. Sherman A. Ross, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 8, 2000, Previously Reported at: 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 3760.
Lawrence v. State, 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 3760 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., June 8, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal by appellants of a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law, Harris County, Texas, convicting them of engaging in homosexual conduct in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.06 (Vernon 1994) and assessing a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were convicted of engaging in homosexual conduct in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.06 (Vernon 1994) and assessed a fine. On appeal, appellants challenged the constitutionality of § 21.06. First, appellants argued § 21.06 violated equal protection guarantees by discriminating both in regard to sexual orientation and gender. The court overruled this argument, because it found that 1) there was no fundamental right to engage in sodomy, 2) homosexuals did not constitute a "suspect class," and 3) the prohibition of homosexual conduct advanced a legitimate state interest and was rationally related thereto, namely, preserving public morals. The court also found that while the statute may adversely affect the conduct of male and female heterosexuals, this did not raise the specter of gender-based discrimination. Second, appellants argued S 21.06 violated the right to privacy guaranteed by both the state and federal constitutions. The court overruled this argument, finding no constitutional "zone of privacy" shielding homosexual conduct from state interference.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; court found that the statute did not offend the equal protection and privacy guarantees assured by both the state and federal constitutions.

Good Shepherd Med. Ctr. v. State


NO. 03-06-00448-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


306 S.W.3d 825; 2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 1184



February 18, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 250TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. D-1-GN-03-003352, HONORABLE LORA J. LIVINGSTON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; Modified and, as Modified, Affirmed in part; Vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical center sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 250th Judicial District (Texas), which dismissed, for lack of standing, its declaratory claims challenging the constitutionality of two statutes. The judgment also ordered that the medical center take nothing against appellees, the State of Texas and others, and granted two intervenors affirmative declarations that the statutes were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The medical center provided services through a preferred provider organization to retired teachers in its area. Two competitors were included in this program, but not in another program for active school district employees. The challenged statutes were amended to prohibit the exclusion of the competitors from either program. Thereafter, one of the competitors was admitted into the program for active school district employees. The court held that the medical center lacked standing to assert a constitutional challenge because it had no contractual right to be the sole provider; rather, its contract expressly contemplated that the program administrator could contract with other hospital providers. Although the medical center argued that the program administrator would not have entered into such contracts but for the amendments, the court found this argument merely speculative. Because the medical center lacked standing, the district court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to adjudicate its claims. Although the medical center failed to brief an issue, thus waiving it under Tex. R. App. P. 38.1(i), the court declined to award sanctions for a frivolous appeal under Tex. R. App. P. 45.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the plea to the jurisdiction and the resulting dismissal for want of subject-matter jurisdiction; vacated the portion of the district court's judgment declaring the amendments constitutional, valid, and enforceable; dismissed the intervenors' claims; and modified the judgment to provide for a dismissal with prejudice instead of a take-nothing judgment.

Combs v. STP Nuclear Operating Co.


NO. 03-06-00428-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


239 S.W.3d 264; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 3468



May 1, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Petition for review denied by STP Nuclear Operating Co. v. Combs, 2008 Tex. LEXIS 840 (Tex., Aug. 29, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a nuclear power plant operator, sued appellant, the Texas Comptroller of Public Accounts, seeking a refund of tax payments made under the independently procured insurance tax, Tex. Ins. Code Ann. § 101.053(b)(4) (Supp. 2006), on grounds that the tax was unconstitutional and violated the McCarran-Ferguson Act. The District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District, Texas, granted the operator summary judgment. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the Comptroller argued that the trial court erred because the State was authorized to collect the independently procured insurance tax (the tax) consistent with due process; equal protection; and the McCarran-Ferguson Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1011 et seq. The appellate court agreed. The tax, as applied to the operator, did not violate either due process or the McCarran-Ferguson Act because the operator was a Texas-based corporation. The taxes for each year at issue, 2002-04, were collected pursuant to insurance contracts that originated, and were negotiated and approved, in Texas. Losses were payable to the owners of the nuclear plant. The tax did not violate the equal protection guarantees of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1-2, Tex. Const. art. I, § 3, and Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1, because the operator did not show that the Comptroller selectively enforced the tax only against domestic corporations. Finally, the statutory scheme imposing the tax was not arbitrary and capricious or unconstitutionally vague. The operator did not argue that the statutory requirements were unconstitutionally vague, and the Comptroller's reporting requirements mirrored the statutory requirements.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's summary judgment and rendered judgment in favor of the Comptroller.

Lilley v. Lilley


NO. 03-00-00284-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


43 S.W.3d 703; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 2351



April 12, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended July 26, 2001. Released for Publication May 31, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 261ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 98-02448, HONORABLE CHARLES F. CAMPBELL, JUDGE PRESIDING. FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 261ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 98-02448, HONORABLE CHARLES F. CAMPBELL, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, Texas that granted appellee grandfather visitation with her daughter, challenging the factual sufficiency of the evidence supporting the order and contending the order violated her due process rights under the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: In their divorce case, the mother and the father had disputed his access to their daughter. After the father committed suicide, the child's paternal grandfather petitioned for visitation with her. Under interim orders, the grandfather was ordered to, and did, obtain grief or anger-management counseling. Before the final hearing, the mother had given the grandfather visitation in excess of what the trial court had ordered. At trial, she testified that contact with the grandfather was in her daughter's best interest. The trial court granted the grandfather visitation on alternate weekends and in the summer. The mother appealed; the appellate court affirmed. The mother did not show that the trial court abused its discretion in granting the grandfather visitation. Though on appeal she claimed the grandfather posed a threat to her daughter, this was inconsistent with positions she had taken earlier. There was no testimony that the grandfather had in any way mistreated the child; his alleged bad acts were years in the past and he had received counseling since then. Nor was Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 153.433 (West Supp. 2001) unconstitutional on its face, or as applied in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ex parte Chamberlain


NO. 2-09-079-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


306 S.W.3d 328; 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 9653



December 17, 2009, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review granted by Ex parte Chamberlain, 2010 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1060 (Tex. Crim. App., Sept. 15, 2010)
Vacated by, Remanded by Ex parte Chamberlain, 2011 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 158 (Tex. Crim. App., Feb. 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 1 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the judgment of the Criminal District Court, No. 1, Tarrant County (Texas) that denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus in relation to sex offender registration requirements.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued, inter alia, that the sex offender registration requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.101 violated substantive due process by imposing on him a compulsory initial registration without any individualized assessment of how dangerous he was or his likelihood of re-offending. The court of appeals disagreed. To the extent that the registration requirements' rational relationship to the State's legitimate interest in protecting its citizens from sex offenders diminished over time, it provided a vehicle for an offender to obtain an individualized assessment of dangerousness and risk of recidivism and possibly obtain early release from his obligation to register as a sex offender. The initial compulsory registration requirement was rationally related to and furthered a legitimate state interest. It contained a mechanism that allowed sex offenders who were purportedly not dangerous and who posed a low risk of re-offending to petition for early termination of the registration requirements. The record was thus insufficient to rebut the presumption that art. 62.101 was constitutional as applied to appellant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Barr v. City of Sinton


NUMBER 13-03-727-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


295 S.W.3d 334; 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 9847



November 23, 2005, Memorandum Opinion Delivered  
November 23, 2005, Memorandum Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Petition for review granted by Barr v. City of Sinton, 2006 Tex. LEXIS 1263 (Tex., Dec. 15, 2006)
Motion granted by Barr v. City of Sinton, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 636 (Tex., July 13, 2007)
Motion denied by Barr v. City of Sinton, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 643 (Tex., July 13, 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Barr v. City of Sinton, 295 S.W.3d 287, 2009 Tex. LEXIS 396 (Tex., June 19, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a pastor and his corporation, challenged a judgment of the 343rd District Court of San Patricio County, Texas, which denied their requested relief in their declaratory action that sought a determination of whether an ordinance adopted by appellee city was constitutional under Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 3a, 6, 8, 27, and whether it violated the Texas Religious Freedom Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 110.001-.012 (2005).


OVERVIEW: Sinton, Tex., Ordinance No. 1999-02 regulated the location of certain correctional and rehabilitation facilities. The pastor owned two homes that were operated to provide housing for parolees and probationers. In affirming, the court noted that an individual's religious beliefs did not excuse him from compliance with an otherwise valid law prohibiting conduct that the State was free to regulate. Because the ordinance was a valid law prohibiting conduct that the city was free to regulate, and because it was generally applicable to any person desiring to operate correctional or rehabilitation facilities, appellants' claims that their freedom of religion rights were violated lacked merit. Nothing in the record established that the city adopted the ordinance to regulate speech because it disagreed with the Christian message the pastor was conveying or with his motivation to clothe, house, and feed the needy. The purpose of the legislation was not to stifle speech, but rather to protect the public by regulating the location of correctional and rehabilitation facilities. Because appellants' religious rights were not substantially burdened by the ordinance, the Act had not been violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In the Interest of E.R.


No. 05-09-01505-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


335 S.W.3d 816; 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 1563



March 3, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 14, 2011.
Petition for review granted by In the Interest of E.R., 2011 Tex. LEXIS 965 (Tex., Dec. 16, 2011)
Motion granted by In the Interest of E.R., 2011 Tex. LEXIS 1009 (Tex., Dec. 22, 2011)
Later proceeding at In re E.R., 2012 Tex. LEXIS 229 (Tex., Mar. 16, 2012)
Reversed by, Remanded by In the Interest of E.R., 2012 Tex. LEXIS 582 (Tex., July 6, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 304th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 06-01398-W.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision of the 304th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which, on a petition filed by appellee Texas Department of Family and Protective Services, terminated her parental rights and denied her motion for a new trial under Tex. R. Civ. P. 329.


OVERVIEW: The mother raised certain issues on appeal, but the court affirmed the termination of her parental rights. The mandatory language of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 161.211 left no room for a construction other than a requirement that any collateral or direct attack on the termination of parental rights, including a motion for new trial, had to be filed no more than six months after the termination order was signed. The court's interpretation of the statutory language of § 161.211 was consistent with the interpretation by other courts of similar language in Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 162.012(a). The six-month deadline in Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 161.211 was not a plea in avoidance, but was a bar to or preclusion of a challenge to a termination order more than six months after the termination order was signed. The court disagreed that the six-month deadline was a statute of limitations affirmative defense that was waived if not pleaded or presented to a trial court. The mother did not argue that her rights were violated or otherwise challenge the constitutionality of the statute and, therefore, she had not preserved or presented the issue for review under Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Ex parte Morales


NO. 03-05-00489-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


212 S.W.3d 483; 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 6321



July 21, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: petition for discretionary review dismd State v. Morales, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 8 (Tex. Crim. App., Jan. 10, 2007)
Petition for discretionary review refused by State v. Morales, 2007 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 131 (Tex. Crim. App., Feb. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR-04-208, HONORABLE GARY L. STEEL, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the 22nd Judicial District Court of Hays County (Texas) that found Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.12 (Supp. 2005) was facially unconstitutional, granted defendant's application for a writ of habeas corpus, and dismissed the indictment of defendant under § 21.12, which prohibited Texas primary and secondary school employees from engaging in sexual conduct with students enrolled at a school where they work.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the indictment against defendant, holding that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.12 was unconstitutional because § 21.12 criminalized sexual conduct not only with minor students, but also with students who were above the age of legal consent. On appeal, the court held that it had jurisdiction to hear the State's appeal because although the State could not appeal an adverse ruling in a habeas proceeding, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.01(a)(1) authorized the State to appeal the dismissal of an indictment. The court found that § 21.12 did not implicate a fundamental right because the concept of privacy rights had not been extended to all adult sexual conduct or intimate relationships generally. The court held that § 21.12 did not violate defendant's due process or equal protection rights because § 21.12 was rationally related to the legitimate state interest in protecting minor students from sexual abuse and exploitation; and the differential treatment of school employees who were married to students versus those who were not also had a rational basis. Also defendant failed to show that § 21.12 was void for vagueness or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court order that held Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.12 was unconstitutional and that dismissed the indictment against defendant, and remanded the case to the trial court for further consistent proceedings.

Tex. Bldg. Owners & Managers Ass'n v. PUC


NO. 03-02-00611-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


110 S.W.3d 524; 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 4710



June 5, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 25, 2003.
Petition for review denied by Tex. Bldg. Owners & Managers Ass'n v. PUC of Tex., 2003 Tex. LEXIS 555 (Tex., Nov. 21, 2003)
Motion for rehearing on petition for review denied by Tex. Bldg. Owners & Managers Ass'n v. PUC, 2004 Tex. LEXIS 3 (Tex., Jan. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. GN200146, HONORABLE DARLENE BYRNE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property management organizations and trade groups (building owners), sued appellee Texas Public Utility Commission, seeking a declaration that the Building Access Statutes of the Public Utility Regulatory Act (PURA), Tex. Util. Code Ann. §§ 54.259-.261 (1998), were unconstitutional. The District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District, Texas, declared the Statutes constitutional. The building owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the building owners contended the Statutes caused a taking of their property without providing an adequate procedure for determining compensation, the Commission lacked the power to determine compensation, and, even if the Commission had that power, it resulted from an unconstitutional delegation. The appellate court disagreed, holding that the legislature designed the Statutes to balance the forces of competition and consumer choice with the rights of property owners to be compensated in the event of a taking. The Statutes expressly delegated to the Commission the power to establish a procedure whereby the building owners could obtain adequate compensation. The provisions granting the Commission jurisdiction to enforce the Statutes delegated to the Commission the power to determine "reasonable" and "nondiscriminatory" compensation when a property owner and telecommunications utility failed to negotiate the amount. Because a lack of adequate procedures to establish compensation was a necessary element to establish a claim under the takings doctrine, the building owners could not have a takings claim until they availed themselves of the Commission's procedures.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Seguin v. Bexar Appraisal Dist.


No. 04-11-00337-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


373 S.W.3d 699; 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 3837



May 16, 2012, Delivered 
May 16, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by Seguin v. Bexar Appraisal Dist., 2013 Tex. LEXIS 365 (Tex., May 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
From the 45th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2009-CI-11323. Honorable Barbara Hanson Nellermoe, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers, a husband and wife, challenged orders of the 45th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, granting summary judgment in favor of appellees, an appraisal district, an appraisal review board, and a chief appraiser, in the taxpayers' action that challenged the district's removal of the disabled veteran tax exemption from property the taxpayers owned after the district discovered the husband was no longer a Texas resident.


OVERVIEW: The husband was a 100 percent permanently disabled United States Army veteran. The court held that in order to be entitled to receive the disabled veteran tax exemption, a disabled veteran had to meet Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.22(g) (Supp. 2011)'s Texas residency requirement. Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2(b) did not create a vested property right in the disabled veteran tax exemption, given the permissive nature of § 2(b) and the fact that it was legislatively revocable. The Texas Legislature had authority to impose Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.22(g)'s residency requirement. Section 11.22(g)'s residency requirement was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose. Accordingly, neither the husband's equal protection rights nor his due process rights were violated. The district and the chief appraiser were not equitably estopped from removing the disabled veteran tax exemption from the taxpayers' property. The chief appraiser had legal authority to remove the tax exemption from the taxpayers' property, and he correctly concluded that, as a nonresident of Texas, the husband was not entitled to the disabled veteran tax exemption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgments of the trial court.
