State ex rel. Lykos v. Fine


NOS. AP-76,470 & AP-76,471


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


330 S.W.3d 904; 2011 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1



January 12, 2011, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON MOTION FOR LEAVE TO FILE PETITION FOR WRIT OF PROHIBITION AND PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS FROM CAUSE NO. 1170853. IN THE 177TH DISTRICT COURT, HARRIS COUNTY.
State ex rel. Lykos v. Fine, 2010 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 735 (Tex. Crim. App., Dec. 7, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with capital murder, and the State gave notice of its intent to seek the death penalty. Defendant filed an "Amended Motion to Declare Article 37.071, § 2 of the Texas Code of Criminal Procedure Unconstitutional as Applied." Respondent, the trial judge of the 177th District Court in Harris County (Texas), commenced an evidentiary hearing on defendant's motion. The State petitioned for mandamus and prohibition relief.


OVERVIEW: The court found defendant was appearing to seek a pretrial ruling from the trial judge that the State was not entitled to proceed with its capital-murder indictment because it was within the realm of possibility that he could be wrongfully convicted and wrongfully sentenced to death if convicted. Because Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.01 did not provide for an appeal by the State of an interlocutory pretrial ruling preventing the State from pursuing a capital-murder conviction and sentence of death, the State had no adequate remedy at law concerning the resolution of defendant's motion. A writ of mandamus or prohibition thus was an appropriate vehicle to review the propriety of defendant's motion and the trial judge's evidentiary hearing. Because there was no basis under Texas law to conduct a pretrial evidentiary hearing to determine the "as applied" constitutionality of a state penal or criminal procedural statute, the trial judge did not have legal authority to conduct any such pretrial evidentiary hearing and make any such pretrial declaratory judgment. He was acting beyond the scope of his lawful authority. Therefore, the State had demonstrated a clear right to relief.


OUTCOME: The court conditionally granted the State mandamus and prohibition relief. If he did not do so himself, the court would order the trial judge to dismiss defendant's amended motion as requesting an unauthorized declaratory judgment.

Univ. of Tex. at El Paso v. Herrera


NO. 08-1049


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


322 S.W.3d 192; 2010 Tex. LEXIS 479; 53 Tex. Sup. J. 956; 159 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,022; 93 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P43,940


March 25, 2010, Argued 
July 2, 2010, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 13, 2010. As Corrected November 15, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE EIGHTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
Univ. of Tex. v. Herrera, 281 S.W.3d 575, 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 8826 (Tex. App. El Paso, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought review of an order from the Court of Appeals for the Eighth District of Texas, which upheld the denial of the employer's plea to the jurisdiction in an action by respondent employee claiming the employer fired him for taking personal medical leave under the self-care provision of the Family and Medical Leave Act (FMLA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 2612(a)(1)(D).


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the employer, a State of Texas university. He sustained an on-the-job injury to his left elbow. He went on leave for approximately nine months. The employer terminated him less than one month after he returned to work. He brought an action against the employer under the FMLA. The employer filed a plea to the jurisdiction, contending it was barred by sovereign immunity. The trial court denied the plea. The court of appeals upheld the decision. On review, the court held that the State could not be sued under the FMLA's self-care provision. As for abrogation, nothing in the legislative record suggested that gender bias by the states was the constitutional evil underlying the self-care provision. The United States Congress exceeded its abrogation authority under § 5 of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 5, when it subjected states to private-damage suits under the self-care provision. A stray line in the employer's policy manual that employees could "bring a civil action against an employer" was insufficient to waive State immunity. The trial court erroneously denied the employer's plea to the jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and dismissed the FMLA claim for lack of subject-matter jurisdiction.

State v. Empey

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An indictment charged defendant with a state jail felony because it alleged that he had stolen aluminum or bronze or copper or brass, of the value of less than $20,000, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(F) (Supp. 2015); the trial court quashed the indictment because § 31.03 could be enforced arbitrarily, such that theft of a copper penny could be a felony and an ounce of gold a misdemeanor; [2]-The court reversed, holding that § 31.03(e)(4)(F) was not unconstitutionally vague because it delegated to prosecutors unfettered discretion to charge a defendant with either a misdemeanor or felony; [3]-No clearly established constitutional prohibition of statutory vagueness was violated although two statutes proscribed the same conduct and defendant was charged under the one subjecting him to greater punishment.


OUTCOME: Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(F) held not facially unconstitutional; trial court's order dismissing the indictment reversed.

 

113 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Henderson v. Love


No. 06-05-00048-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


181 S.W.3d 810; 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 9886


September 7, 2005, Submitted  
November 30, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 115th Judicial District Court, Marion County, Texas. Trial Court No. 0400170.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant buyer sought review of a summary judgment of the 115th Judicial District Court, Marion County (Texas), in favor of appellee seller in the buyer's action to recover liquidated damages under Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 5.077 based on the seller's failure to provide an annual report on certain financial details of the parties' executory contract of sale.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that § 5.077, as applied, violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 16. The court agreed that Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 5.077 was constitutionally suspect as a possible impairment of the obligation of the parties' contract. As amended in 2001, the language of § 5.077, considered alone, could exact on the parties' contract a penalty grossly in excess of the value of the entire contract, which financed little more than five percent of the potential penalty. Section 5.077 also potentially imposed an excessive fine, in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 41.004(a) provided, however, that, before exemplary damages could be recovered, more-than-nominal actual damages had to be awarded to the claimant. Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 41.008(b) also limited such exemplary damages to no more than the greater of (a) $ 200,000, or (b) any noneconomic damages found by a jury not to exceed $ 750,000, plus double the amount of economic damages. Those restrictions would dramatically limit the Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 5.077 penalty and impose as a condition precedent that actual damages be proven, thus making § 5.077 constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

R. M. v. State ex rel. Tex. Dep't of State Health Servs.


NO. 03-08-00317-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 7242



September 26, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
FROM THE PROBATE COURT NO. 1 OF TRAVIS COUNTY. NO. 95,519, HONORABLE GUY S. HERMAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient appealed the judgment of the Probate Court No. 1, Travis County (Texas) that ordered the administration of psychoactive medication under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 574.104.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued, inter alia, that probate court's findings of fact and conclusions of law were insufficient to deprive him of his "liberty" from forced medication because the probate court did not find that he was dangerous. The court of appeals disagreed. The patient was not released on bail but committed to the hospital. A psychiatrist testified to the patient's present mental condition and his threats at the hospital "to get us all killed," and that he was "confrontational with other patients" and "with the staff." The patient's mother testified that she had daily contact with her son over the last year and that he could be a danger to himself and others because he "stopped the medication." Based on that evidence, the court of appeals could presume a finding of dangerous in support of the probate court's order. The psychiatrist's application to medicate the patient was brought as part of the patient's treatment program in an inpatient mental health facility--not solely to render the patient competent to stand trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ford Motor Co. v. Sheldon


No. 98-0539


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


22 S.W.3d 444; 2000 Tex. LEXIS 48; 43 Tex. Sup. J. 719


February 9, 1999, Argued  
May 11, 2000, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] For RESPONDENT: Pereira, Mr. Andres Christian, Fleming & Associates, Houston, TX, Bonilla, Mr. Jonathan R., Bonilla Ogle & Perschbach, Corpus, Christi, TX, Bonilla, Mr. William D., Law Offices of William D. Bonilla, Corpus Christi, TX, Bonilla & Chapa, Corpus, Christi, TX, Kesler, Mr. Christopher A., Fleming & Associates, Houston, TX, Davidow, Ms. Sylvia, Fleming & Associates, Houston, TX.
On remand at, Remanded by Ford Motor Co. v. Sheldon, 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 6926 (Tex. App. Austin, Aug. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRD DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
Ford Motor Co. v. Sheldon, 965 S.W.2d 65, 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1476 (Tex. App. Austin, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner automobile manufacturer and distributors appealed a Court of Appeals for the Third District of Texas decision granting class certification, but modifying the trial court's class definition, in a case where respondent purchasers allegedly sustained damages because of peeling paint on vehicles purchased from petitioners.


OVERVIEW: Respondent purchasers brought actions under multiple theories, individually and on behalf of all others similarly situated, against petitioner automobile manufacturer and distributors. Respondents alleged petitioners' actions in removing spray primer from the paint process caused the paint to prematurely peel on particular vehicles purchased by respondents. The trial court identified the class as those individuals whose vehicles had suffered or would suffer peeling because of defective paint or who had petitioners' repairs because of defective paint. The appellate court modified the class because the trial court's definition would have required a determination of the merits. It defined the class as those who had problems or had repairs because the alleged peeling was due to defective paint. Petitioners appealed. The court established it had jurisdiction, then reversed and remanded the case. The court held that neither court met the requirement that the class be clearly ascertainable by reference to objective criteria.


OUTCOME: Court of appeals' judgment reversed and case remanded to the trial court to decertify respondent purchasers' class because neither the trial court nor the court of appeals properly defined the class members because the class members were not clearly ascertainable by reference to objective criteria.

In the Interest of J.M.D.


NO. 14-03-01196-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 2510



March 30, 2006, Judgment Rendered  
March 30, 2006, Memorandum Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Petition for review denied by In the Interest of J.M.D., 2006 Tex. LEXIS 695 (Tex., July 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 312th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Cause No. 80-06931.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of an order of the 312th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted judgment for child-support arrearages in favor of appellee ex-wife and denied the ex-husband's motion for new trial. The ex-husband asserted, in part, that the underlying child-support judgment was dormant and had not been timely revived and that an amendment to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 158.102 (2002) violated his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The divorce decree required the ex-husband to pay to the ex-wife monthly child support each month, but he never paid any support. The court first noted that the 1980 divorce decree, which ordered him to pay support, was not a child-support judgment. Thus, because the ex-husband's child-support arrearages were not reduced to a judgment until July 2003, his dormancy argument pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 34.001 (1997) failed. The court next determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the ex-husband's motion for new trial based on the defenses of waiver and laches where he did not present evidence to establish those defenses at the hearing on the ex-wife's motion for enforcement. Finally, the court rejected the ex-husband's argument that the amendment to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 158.102 (2002) violated his due-process and due-course-of-law rights as well as protections against retroactive laws under the United States Constitution and Tex. Const. art. I, § 16. The court held that legislation amending statutes to extend time limits within which enforcement of an existing child-support liability could be effected did not violate § 16.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

117 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Tex. Mun. League v. Tex. Workers' Comp. Comm'n


NO. 00-1114


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


74 S.W.3d 377; 2002 Tex. LEXIS 38; 45 Tex. Sup. J. 533


September 19, 2001, Argued  
April 4, 2002, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRD DISTRICT OF TEXAS.

Texas Workers' Compensation Comm'n v. Texas Mun. League Intergovernmental Risk Pool, 38 S.W.3d 591, 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 6310 (Tex. App. Austin 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a joint-insurance risk pool that provided workers' compensation benefits to municipal employees, obtained a declaratory judgment that statutory requirements to pay its unclaimed death benefits to the Texas Workers' Compensation Subsequent Injury Fund were unconstitutional. On appeal by defendant, the Texas Workers' Compensation Commission, the Court of Appeals for the Third District of Texas reversed. The risk pool appealed.


OVERVIEW: The risk pool, which provided workers' compensation benefits to municipal employees in more than 1,600 Texas cities, contended on appeal that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 403.007(a) and 408.184(c), as applied, violated Tex. Const. art III § 52(a) and Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1-e , because they either required Texas cities to make gratuitous payments of public money, or because they imposed a statewide ad valorem tax. The supreme court held that the provisions were constitutional. Disagreeing with the court of appeals, the supreme court held that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 403.007(a) and 408.184(c) were not analogous to custodial-escheat statutes. The supreme court held that the challenged provisions did not require the risk pool to gratuitously grant public money, because the member cities received consideration from the fund, and the provisions served a legitimate public purpose with a clear public benefit. It also held that the challenged provisions did not effectively levy a 100 percent ad valorem tax on the unclaimed death benefits, but only transferred unclaimed benefits that the risk pools' member cities already committed to paying workers' compensation claims.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals.

 

118 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Tex. Dep't of Family & Protective Servs. v. Dickensheets


NO. 01-07-00584-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


274 S.W.3d 150; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 6892



September 11, 2008, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 300th District Court, Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 35600.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas Department of Family and Protective Services (DFPS) challenged a decision from the 300th District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, which dismissed a termination of parental rights proceeding filed against appellee parents. A motion to dismiss the appeal was filed.


OVERVIEW: In a suit affecting the parent and child relationship (SAPCR), the parental grandparents of a minor child were given a temporary managing conservatorship. Termination proceedings against the parents were dismissed, and the DFPS appealed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that a dismissal of the appeal was not warranted. There was a final, appealable order under former Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 263.401(d) due to the entry of the order concerning the grandparents. Next, former § 263.401 did not violate the separation of powers clause under Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. There was no unconstitutional interference with the State's performance of its prosecutorial function. In enacting the 12-month dismissal date for State-initiated termination proceedings, the Texas Legislature was not attempting to speed up the prosecutor's preparation and ultimate readiness for trial. Rather, it was providing guidelines for assuring that Texas children were returned to their parents or adopted as quickly as possible. Refiling the SAPCR with new facts demonstrating that the return of the child to the parents would endanger him did not unduly interfere with the State's prosecutorial function.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed. The motion to dismiss the appeal was denied.

State v. Markovich


NO. 1979-00


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


77 S.W.3d 274; 2002 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 113



May 29, 2002, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPELLEE'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM THE THIRD DISTRICT COURT OF APPEALS. TRAVIS COUNTY.
 State v. Markovich, 34 S.W.3d 21, 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 7022 (Tex. App. Austin 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the Class B misdemeanor offense of disrupting a meeting or procession. Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.05. He filed a pre-trial motion to quash the complaint by attacking the constitutionality of § 42.05. The trial court granted his motion. The State appealed. The Third District Court of Appeals, Travis County (Texas) reversed the trial judge's decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant disrupted a Presidential speech by standing up and shouting, causing the U.S. President to stop speaking, substantially impairing the ordinary conduct of the meeting. On appeal the State argued that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.05 was not impermissibly vague, it gave police officers and others of ordinary intelligence reasonable notice of what was proscribed. The instant court concluded the Court of Appeals did not err in concluding the curtailment of others' First Amendment rights was not intended to be included as a part of the narrowing construction expounded in caselaw. The statute was not vague on its face. It did not require police officers or citizens to know and apply delicate issues of First Amendment jurisprudence. It simply prohibited individuals from intentionally engaging in behavior that disrupted or prevented the ordinary conduct of a meeting. As the Third Court of Appeals correctly asserted, whether a person's conduct substantially impaired the ordinary conduct of a meeting was an objective standard that did not acquire its meaning from a particular officer's determination of what constituted substantial impairment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Third Court of Appeals was affirmed.

HEB Ministries, Inc. v. Tex. Higher Educ. Coordinating Bd.


NO. 03-01-00103-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


114 S.W.3d 617; 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 6321



July 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 2, 2003.
Petition for review granted by HEB Ministries, Inc. v. Tex. Higher Educ. Coordinating Bd., 2004 Tex. LEXIS 1458 (Tex., Dec. 3, 2004)
Reversed by, Remanded by HEB Ministries, Inc. v. Tex. Higher Educ. Coordinating Bd., 235 S.W.3d 627, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 800 (Tex., Aug. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 98-09152, HONORABLE PAUL DAVIS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, Reversed in part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant religious school brought a declaratory action against appellee Texas Higher Education Coordinating Board raising facial constitutional challenges to Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 61.304, .313 (1996 & Supp. 2003). The District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District, Texas, ruled unconstitutional the provision regulating the use of the term "seminary" and upheld the regulation of the granting of degrees. The school appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the school contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to declare Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 61.304 (1996) unconstitutional. The board contended that the trial court erred by declaring regulation of the term "seminary" by Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 61.313(a)(1) (Supp. 2003) a violation of the First Amendment to the U.S. Constitution and Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 6, 8, 29. The appellate court ruled that the regulation of the term "seminary" under Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 61.313 (Supp. 2003) was content-neutral and served a significant governmental interest. Further, § 61.313 was narrowly tailored to further the board's interest in preventing the fraudulent use of academic terms by private postsecondary institutions; it did not violate the Free Speech Clause of the First Amendment. The appellate court also ruled that Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 61.304 (1996) satisfied all three requirements of Lemon and did not violate the Establishment Clause of the U.S. Constitution by fostering excessive government entanglement with religion.


OUTCOME: That portion of judgment ruling that regulating the granting of degrees was constitutional was affirmed. That portion of the judgment declaring regulation of the term "seminary" as unconstitutional was reversed, and judgment was rendered that such regulation was not unconstitutional. The board's administrative penalty against the schools was reinstated.

Villarreal v. State


NUMBERS 13-05-123-CR & 13-05-124-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI - EDINBURG


267 S.W.3d 204; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 5132

July 3, 2008, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISH. TEX. R. APP. P. 47.2(b).


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On appeal from the County Court at Law No. 4 of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 4 of Nueces County, Texas, convicting her of offending a state law prohibiting the sale of obscene devices, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23(c)(1) (2003) and offending a municipal ordinance prohibiting the operation of a sexually oriented business without a permit, Corpus Christi, Tex., Code of Ordinances ch. 48, art. I, § 48-18(b) (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a sales clerk at an adult store, was arrested and convicted for selling a vibrator to an undercover police officer. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's claim that Tex. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Wright v. State


NO. PD-0513-05


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


201 S.W.3d 765; 2006 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1818



September 20, 2006, Delivered  
September 20, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PUBLISH


PRIOR HISTORY: ON THE STATE'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM THE ELEVENTH COURT OF APPEALS. TAYLOR COUNTY.
Wright v. State, 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 377 (Tex. App. Eastland, Jan. 20, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of methamphetamine of less than 400 grams but more than 200 grams. The Eleventh Court of Appeals, Taylor County (Texas) affirmed defendant's conviction on remand. The court granted defendant's petition for discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant originally appealed her conviction, claiming that the evidence was insufficient to prove that the aggregate weight of the substance possessed was more than 200 grams and that Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.002(5) was unconstitutional. The appellate court was directed to conduct a statutory construction analysis of the statute. The appellate court affirmed. On review, the court agreed that the appellate court did not undertake a sufficient statutory construction analysis and the court resolved the issues, affirming the conviction. The appellate court failed to determine whether the language in § 481.002(5) produced an absurd result, namely defendant's conviction. In addressing the matter, the court found no absurd result. The toxic liquid mixed with the methamphetamine in this case was a necessary part of the manufacturing process. It did not lead to an absurd result to include the unusable toxic liquids in the aggregate weight of the controlled substance. Under the statute, evidence indicating that a mixture contained a controlled substance was sufficient to support the conviction for possession in an amount equal to the aggregate weight of the mixture.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Liberty Mut. Ins. Co. v. Tex. Dep't of Ins.


NO. 03-04-00105-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


187 S.W.3d 808; 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 1681



March 3, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 2006.
Petition for review denied by Liberty Mut. Ins. Co. v. Tex. Dep't of Ins., 2006 Tex. LEXIS 1241 (Tex., Dec. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-08264, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant insurers challenged a judgment of the District Court of Travis County (Texas) that denied the insurers' motion for summary judgment in their declaratory action and held that a rule of appellee Texas Department of Insurance that required the insurers to rebate reinsurance surpluses to policyholders was valid. The policyholders had filed suit against the insurers seeking a share of the surpluses.


OVERVIEW: The insurers claimed that Texas Department of Insurance Order No. 97-0738 (the 1997 rule) that required the insurers to rebate reinsurance surpluses in 1991 and 1992 to policyholders deprived them of their contractual rights, of property without due process, and was an unconstitutional retroactive law. The court found that the 1997 rule implemented the directive of former Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 5.76-2, § 4.04 that deficits and surpluses of the Texas Workers' Compensation Assigned Risk Facility were to be passed on to policyholders. The court held that the 1997 rule and the factors specified in Department letters did not unconstitutionally impair the insurers' contractual rights because they could not have reasonably expected that they could retain the surpluses after they had been relieved of the obligation of covering the deficits. The court found that the 1997 rule did not deprive the insurers' of property without due process and was not an unconstitutional retroactive law because it rationally furthered the legitimate state purpose of preserving the workers' compensation market and there was no prior law that allowed insurers to pass through deficits and retain surpluses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Johnson v. Jackson Walker, L.L.P.


No. 05-06-00121-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


247 S.W.3d 765; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 1663



March 6, 2008, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 26, 2008.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 416th Judicial District Court, Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 416-2289-03.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shareholder sued defendant directors on behalf of defendant corporation under Tex. Bus. Corp. Act Ann. art. 5.14 (2003). He amended his pleadings to add himself individually as a party plaintiff and to seek the appointment of a receiver over the corporation. The 416th Judicial District Court, Collin County, Texas, denied his motion for a receiver, and dismissed his derivative claim. He appealed in his representative capacity.


OVERVIEW: Among the various challenges to article 5.14, raised by the shareholder, all of which were rejected by the appellate court, he argued that the statute was unconstitutional, both facially and as applied to his circumstances. Like his other claims, there was no merit to his constitutional claims. Article 5.14 did not violate the separation of powers guarantee in Tex. Const. art. II, § 1, because it did not unconstitutionally delegate judicial power to a nonjudicial officer--i.e., the special litigation committee--without appropriate safeguards or opportunity for judicial review. Nor did the statute violate the due process of law guarantee in Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, because the shareholder did not have a property interest at stake, and any recovery in the derivative action belonged to the corporation. The statute did not violate the guarantee of equal protection in Tex. Const. art. I, § 3. Nor did it violate the open court's provision in Tex. Const. art. I, § 13; or the guarantee of trial by jury in Tex. Const. art. I, § 15, since his action was in equity, not in law. The shareholder waived appellate review of his remaining constitutional claims.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

TXU Generation Co., L.P. v. PUC of Tex.


NO. 03-04-00148-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


165 S.W.3d 821; 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 3771



May 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by TXU Generation Co. LP v. PUC of Tex., 2006 Tex. LEXIS 1091 (Tex., Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE PUBLIC UTILITY COMMISSION OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, market participants, and intervenor, a market participant, sought review of an order of the Public Utility Commission of Texas, which, pursuant to Tex. Util. Code Ann. § 39.001(e) of the Public Utilities Regulation Act, adopted the Wholesale Market Oversight Rule (WMO Rule), 16 Tex. Admin. Code § 25.503, governing the Commission's oversight of the competitive wholesale electricity market.


OVERVIEW: The Commission established the WMO Rule to articulate standards that the Commission would apply in monitoring the activities of those participating in the wholesale electricity markets. The Commission defined the duties of market participants and those activities which were prohibited. The court held that the Commission possessed the statutory authority to enact the WMO Rule under Tex. Util. Code Ann. §§ 35.004(e) and 39.157 (Supp. 2004-2005). The WMO Rule balanced the competing statutory obligations of establishing a competitive market for electricity and ensuring safe, reliable, and reasonably priced power for consumers and ancillary services by allowing market forces to set the price of electricity but prohibiting market manipulation and activities that would materially affect reliability. The rule was not unconstitutionally vague. The broad language in the definition of prohibited activities was tempered by the availability of a defense when a market participant had acted in accordance with Electric Reliability Council of Texas protocols or had pursued a legitimate business purpose and exercised due diligence to avoid an adverse effect on prices, reliability, and accounting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's order adopting the rule.

Scott v. State


Nos. PD-1069-09 & PD-1070-09


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


322 S.W.3d 662; 2010 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1249; 38 Media L. Rep. 2548



October 6, 2010, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Scott v. Texas, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 3155 (U.S., Apr. 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON THE STATE'S PETITION FOR DISCRETIONARY REVIEW FROM THE FOURTH COURT OF APPEALS, BEXAR COUNTY.
Scott v. State, 298 S.W.3d 264, 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 4726 (Tex. App. San Antonio, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Court of Appeals, Bexar County (Texas), reversed defendant's conviction of two counts of harassment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07, holding that the terms "annoy," "alarm," "abuse," "torment," "embarrass," and "repeated" contained in § 42.07(a)(4) and (a)(7) were unconstitutionally vague. The State petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: Section 42.07(a)(4) did not implicate the free-speech guarantee of the First Amendment because it was directly only at people who, with the specific intent to inflict emotional distress, repeatedly used the telephone to invade another person's personal privacy, and did so in a manner reasonably likely to inflict emotional distress. Therefore, the conduct falling within § 42.07(a)(4) would usually be essentially noncommunicative conduct, even if the conduct included spoken words, as people whose conduct violated the statute would not have an intent to engage in the legitimate communication of ideas, opinions, or information but rather would have only the intent to inflict emotional distress for its own sake. To the extent that § 42.07(a)(4) was susceptible of application to communicative conduct, it was susceptible of such application only when that conduct was not protected by the First Amendment because it invaded the privacy interests of the victim in an intolerable manner. Because § 42.07(a)(4) did not implicate the First Amendment, defendant was required to show that it was unduly vague as applied to his own conduct; as he failed to do so, his vagueness challenge failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Ex parte Perez


No. 05-03-00363-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 4670



June 3, 2003, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 3. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. WX02-00081-J.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, accused, was charged with the offense of unlawfully carrying a firearm, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02 (2003), and filed a pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus, seeking dismissal of the charge. The Criminal District Court No. 3 for Dallas County, Texas, denied the accused the relief he sought, and the accused appealed.


OVERVIEW: The accused argued that the trial court erred in denying him the requested relief on the grounds that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02 was unconstitutional. The accused asserted that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02 violated the Second Amendment, as that amendment was applied to the State of Texas through the Fourteenth Amendment. The State responded that the accused's concession that existing case law out of the U.S. Supreme Court was contrary to his position ended the analysis and that the appellate court was bound by the Supreme Court's pronouncement on the issue. The appellate court agreed with the State's argument, as the Supreme Court stated that the Second Amendment guaranteed no right to keep and bear a firearm that did not have some reasonable relationship to the preservation or efficiency of a well regulated militia. Also, the appellate court observed no reason to depart from holdings by the federal courts of appeals that the Ninth Amendment did not provide a separate individual right to bear arms. Furthermore, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02 bore a rational relationship to the State's interest in preventing crime and was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dean v. State


NO. 14-00-00303-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


60 S.W.3d 217; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 5564



August 16, 2001, Rendered  
August 16, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 177th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 826,526. Davis, Carol, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Without entering into a plea agreement, defendant pled guilty to the offense of indecency with a child. The 177th District Court, Harris County, Texas, assessed punishment at 10 years in prison. Defendant was also required to register as a sex offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended the 1999 amendments to the Texas Sex Offender Registration Program (Act), Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.01 et seq. (Vernon Supp. 2001) requiring registration as a sex offender violated the ex post facto clause of the U.S. Constitution. Defendant exposed himself to an eight-year-old child in May 1999. The public disclosure amendments were effective September 1999. The appeals court initially concluded the Texas Legislature did not have a primary intent to punish sex offenders by enacting the 1999 amendments to the Act. In other words, the amended disclosure provisions did not transform what was clearly intended as a civil remedy into a criminal penalty. The amended disclosure provisions imposed no specific affirmative disability or restraint on the offender. The limitations on public disclosure in the Act strongly indicated that the Act is tailored to address specific governmental interests of public protection. The appeals courts ultimately found the Act and its 1999 amendments did not violate the ex post facto clause.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Hendee v. Dewhurst


NO. 03-06-00501-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


228 S.W.3d 354; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 4149



May 25, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 28, 2008.

As Corrected May 6, 2008.
Motion granted by Dewhurst v. Hendee, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 542 (Tex., June 11, 2007)
Petition for review denied by Dewhurst v. Hendee, 2007 Tex. LEXIS 635 (Tex., July 10, 2007)
Writ of mandamus granted In re Hendee, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 10172 (Tex. App. Austin, Aug. 27, 2007)
Appeal after remand at Dewhurst v. Hendee, 253 S.W.3d 320, 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 2422 (Tex. App. Austin, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. D-1-GN-06-002156, HONORABLE WILLIAM E. BENDER, JUDGE PRESIDING.
Hendee v. Dewhurst, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 3078 (Tex. App. Austin, Apr. 17, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; Reversed and Remanded in part on Motion for Rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a citizen and a citizen group, appealed a judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District (Texas), granting a plea to jurisdiction filed by defendants, the Lieutenant Governor, the Speaker of the House of Representatives, the Comptroller, members of the Legislative Budget Board, and the State of Texas, and dismissing plaintiffs' claims filed under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 37.001-.011 (2006).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendants, alleging that H.B. 1, 79th Leg. (Tex. 2005) was unconstitutional because its appropriation caused defendants to exceed the aggregate biennial cap on the rate of growth of appropriations under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 22 and Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 316.001 (2005). On appeal the court held that the district court properly dismissed plaintiffs' claim that H.B. 1 was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative powers because the only delegation of legislative power that plaintiffs attacked was merely an assignment of duties within the legislative branch akin to each chamber's referral of bills to committees prior to consideration before the entire chamber. The district court erred by dismissing plaintiffs' claims seeking declarations that future expenditures under H.B. 1 would be unconstitutional. Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 22 was self-executing to the extent of prohibiting legislative action inconsistent with its provisions, and plaintiffs claims of violations did not present non-justiciable political questions. The dispositive issues controlling whether plaintiffs had validly pleaded each theory was not raised, briefed, or developed in the district court.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing plaintiffs' claim alleging unconstitutional delegation of legislative powers for want of jurisdiction was affirmed. To the extent that plaintiffs' remaining two claims sought declarations that future expenditures under H.B.1's appropriation were unconstitutional or illegal, the district court abused its discretion in dismissing those claims, and those portions of the district court's judgment were reversed.

Montpas v. State


No. 05-99-00461-CR, No. 05-99-00462-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 489

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions for operating a motor vehicle without proof of financial responsibility and without current registration from the County Criminal Court of Appeals, Dallas County (Texas), which affirmed the judgment of the municipal court in a bench trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of operating a motor vehicle without proof of financial responsibility and without current registration in a bench trial to the municipal court. The county criminal court of appeals affirmed. The appellate court affirmed, holding that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 30.01 (Supp. 2000) did not prohibit the municipal judge from adjudicating traffic offenses which, by their nature, there was no injured party. The appellate court further rejected appellant's argument that the Garland Municipal Court of Record Act (Act) denied him due process by its very "complexity," holding that the Act simplified the process for the appellant by containing in a single statute most of the rules and procedures needed by an appellant to the county court whereas the procedures for appeals from municipal courts not of record are spread over a myriad of statutes and rules.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed traffic convictions in the municipal court of record, holding that Texas law prohibiting a judge from adjudicating proceedings in which the judge was an injured party did not prohibit a municipal judge from adjudicating traffic offenses.

Stewart v. State


NO. 14-98-00451-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


13 S.W.3d 127; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 748



February 3, 2000, Rendered  
February 3, 2000, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 30, 2000. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused August 30, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 209th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-00619. Hon. Michael McSpadden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a challenge to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 44.29 as a violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV following his re-sentencing by the 209th District Court, Harris County (Texas) for aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review following his resentencing for aggravated robbery alleging Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 44.29 violated the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 44.29 provided that if an appellate court awarded a new trial to a defendant only on the basis of an error or errors made in the punishment state of the trial, the court shall commence the new trial as if a finding of guilt had been returned and proceed to the punishment stage of the trial. Affirming, the court held standard for appellate review for U.S. Const. amend. XIV was to determine whether the classification bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. Limiting a remedy to the phase of the trial where the error occurred was a rational state interest; thus, appellant was not entitled to a new trial regarding his conviction.


OUTCOME: Affirmed; limiting appellant's remedy to the phase of the trial where the error occurred was rationally related to legitimate state interest; legitimate state interest being the standard of appellate review under the Equal Protection Clause, appellant was only entitled to retrial where the error occurred not a complete new trial.

Hendee v. Dewhurst


NO. 03-06-00501-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 3078



April 17, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at, Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing overruled by, Reconsideration denied by Hendee v. Dewhurst, 228 S.W.3d 354, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 4149 (Tex. App. Austin, May 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 345TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. D-1-GN-06-002156, HONORABLE WILLIAM E. BENDER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, Reversed and Remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an organization and its director, brought a declaratory judgment action against defendants, including the State of Texas and the Legislative Budget Board (LBB), in Travis County District Court, 345th Judicial District (Texas), alleging that an appropriations bill violated Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 22(a) and Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 316.001 (2005). The district court granted defendants' plea to the jurisdiction. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appropriation bill made certain school funding appropriations. Plaintiffs alleged that the bill caused the rate of growth of appropriations to exceed the aggregate biennial cap under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 22(a) and Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 316.001. Plaintiffs claimed that the method used under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 316.002 (2005) for establishing the cap was inconsistent with Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 22(a); they also claimed that delegation of authority to the LBB violated separation-of-powers limitations and that the additional appropriations exceeded even the LBB's calculations of the cap. The court of appeals found that Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 22 was self-executing to the extent of prohibiting legislative action inconsistent with its standards, and plaintiffs' claims that the standards had been violated did not present a non-justiciable political question. Plaintiffs could not allege a violation of separation of powers based on assignments of duties within the legislative branch. Taxpayer standing existed to challenge future expenditures under the appropriation. However, plaintiffs failed to sufficiently allege associational standing on the part of the organization.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed as to plaintiffs' separation-of-powers claim; the judgment was reversed as to the remaining claims. Plaintiffs were entitled to leave to amend regarding the organization's standing.

Ex parte Kubas


NUMBER 13-00-633-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


83 S.W.3d 366; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 5625



August 1, 2002, Opinion Delivered  
August 1, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1] PUBLISH. TEX. R. APP. P. 47.3.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 347th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for habeas corpus relief in the 347th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, alleging that the statutory requirement that he register as a sex offender for a ten-year period after his discharge from community supervision was an unlawful restraint of his liberty in violation of the provisions of Tex. Const. art.1, § 16. The trial court denied relief and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been placed on deferred adjudication supervision for five years following his guilty plea to attempted sexual assault. As a condition of supervision, defendant was required to register as a sex offender under the provisions of the Texas Sex Offender Registration Program. Eight months before defendant was successfully discharged from supervision, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 62.11, 62.12(b)(2) (Vernon Supp. 2002) were amended to include defendant in a class of persons required to register for 10 years after release. Defendant registered during the time he was on supervision and for a brief period afterwards, but argued that the requirement that he continue to register violated the provisions of Tex. Const. art.1, § 16, against retroactive laws. The appellate court held that the amendments were not unconstitutional as applied to defendant. The program was remedial in nature, not punitive, and defendant's rights did not vest until his release from supervision. As the amendments took effect prior to defendant's release, they were not retroactive as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Tex. Alcoholic Bev. Comm'n v. Silver City Club


No. 05-09-00422-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


315 S.W.3d 643; 2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 4345



June 10, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 6, 2010.
Rehearing overruled by Tex. Alcoholic Bev. Comm'n v. Silver City Club, 2010 Tex. App. LEXIS 6398 (Tex. App. Dallas, July 28, 2010)
Petition for review denied by Silver City Club v. Tex. Alcoholic Bev. Comm'n, 2011 Tex. LEXIS 167 (Tex., Feb. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 101st District Court, Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 09-02690-E, 09-04675-E.
Illusions - Dallas Private Club Inc. v. Steen, 320 Fed. Appx. 274, 2009 U.S. App. LEXIS 7559 (5th Cir. Tex., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Texas Alcoholic Beverage Commission, sought review of a judgment of the 101st District Court, Dallas County, Texas, declaring Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 32.03(k) void for violating Tex. Const. art. III, § 35(a), and reversing the Commission's order refusing to renew a permit of appellee, a private club, to serve alcohol at their sexually oriented business.


OVERVIEW: Section 32.03(k) prohibited the Commission from issuing or renewing a private club registration permit for a club in a dry area that operated a sexually oriented business. The club had challenged the Commission's order pursuant to Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 11.67 and 32.18. The Commission argued on appeal that the trial court erred in determining that the enactment of § 32.03(k) violated the single subject rule of Article III. On review, the court reversed, concluding by required liberal construction under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 311.021(1) that § 32.03(k) did not violate the single subject rule because the bill all related, at least indirectly, under the common subject of government reform as required by the bill's title. The fact that the bill covered many different codes and areas of law did not violate the requirement of Article III, § 35, that the bill contain no more than one subject. Therefore, the trial court erred, and the court sustained the Commission's issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and rendered judgment that the Commission's order refusing the renewal permit application was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant practicing orthotics sought review from a judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee Texas State Board of Orthotics & Prosthetics in the orthotics' declaratory judgment action, and declared that rules passed by the Board regarding licensing under the Orthotics and Prosthetics Act, Tex. The court applied similar reasoning to find 22 Tex. Admin. Code § 821.15 (2003) invalid with respect to the exemption for "unique qualifications."

Bexar Metro. Water Dist. v. City of San Antonio


NO. 03-06-00557-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


228 S.W.3d 887; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 5081



June 29, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. D-1-GV-06-000053, HONORABLE SCOTT H. JENKINS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a water district and others, challenged a summary judgment entered by the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District, Texas, for appellee water system in the system's suit seeking a declaration that the district was prohibited from expanding its political boundaries and service area past certain geographical limits described in its enabling statute, as amended by Senate Bill 1494, Tex. Gen. Laws 1593 (SB 1494).


OVERVIEW: Because the system alleged that the district's actions were void and because the system, in seeking to provide water-utility services in the same area as the district, was an affected person, the court found that the system had standing to bring its suit for declaratory judgment. The court held that the enactment of SB 1494 did not violate the Texas Constitution. SB 1494 did not add additional land to the district's political territory or alter its taxing authority. As a result, SB 1494 was not subject to the notice provisions of Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 59. In light of the legislature's restriction in SB 1494 of the district's water service to areas "within the district," the legislative history indicating that the phrase "within and without" was considered and subsequently abandoned, and the repeal of the only procedures for expansion available under the district's enabling statute, 1945 Tex. Gen. Laws 491, the court concluded that the district's political boundaries and service area were restricted to the geographic area described in the enabling statute, as amended by § 3 of SB 1494.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

144 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Dill v. Fowler


No. 11-07-00227-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


255 S.W.3d 681; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 2667



April 10, 2008, Decided 
April 10, 2008, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 35th District Court, Brown County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. CV0507318.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant survivors sought review of a summary judgment from the 35th District Court, Brown County (Texas), which dismissed medical malpractice claims against appellee doctors.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was taken to an emergency room suffering from internal bleeding and died shortly after surgery. The survivors produced no evidence of wilful and wanton negligence. The doctors argued that because the decedent was in a medical emergency when he arrived at the hospital, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.153 (2005) applied, and the case could not be maintained without evidence of wilful and wanton negligence. The survivors challenged the constitutionality of § 74.153 on equal protection grounds. The court held that the application of § 74.153 did not violate the equal protection guarantee of Tex. Const. art. I, § 3 because a rational basis existed for imposing a lower standard of care when a patient was receiving emergency care. Because a medical malpractice crisis was interfering with the overall delivery of health-care services and because there were additional issues unique to emergency medical services, the legislature could appropriately address these concerns by lowering the standard of care for emergency medical services. The legislature could rationally determine that increased availability of emergency care would result.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re M.A.H.


NO. 2-99-048-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


20 S.W.3d 860; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 4072



June 15, 2000, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Granted and Affirmed on Rehearing June 15, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of April 20, 2000, Previously Reported at: 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 2901.

FROM THE 323RD DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged decision from the 323rd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), finding that appellant engaged in delinquent conduct by committing two instances of indecency and requiring appellant to register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing before the court, the trial court found that appellant juvenile engaged in delinquent conduct by committing two instances of indecency with a child. As a result, appellant was required to register as a sex offender pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 62.01(5)(H) (2000). Appellant complained the Sex Offender Registration Program violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection of the laws. The court affirmed. After applying a rational basis test, the court concluded the registration and notification statutes bore a rational relationship to the State's interests. Appellant's right to equal protection of the laws was not violated merely because he was treated differently from another person who commits different, although similar, conduct charged under a different statute. Because appellant was treated the same as all similarly situated nonviolent sex offenders for purposes of the duration of the registration requirements, appellant's argument failed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment was affirmed. Registration and notification statutes bore a rational relationship to State's interests, and appellant's due process and equal protection right were not violated.

Johnson v. State


NO. 09-11-00429-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


2013 Tex. App. LEXIS 321


November 6, 2012, Submitted 
January 16, 2013, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE: PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing overruled by Johnson v. State, 2013 Tex. App. LEXIS 2242 (Tex. App. Beaumont, Mar. 6, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
On Appeal from the 359th District Court, Montgomery County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 11-05-05840-CR.
Johnson v. State, 2006 Tex. App. LEXIS 8299 (Tex. App. Beaumont, Sept. 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 359th District Court, Montgomery County, Texas, which convicted him of failing to register, as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.051(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of failing to register based on a failure to report within 7 days. He entered a plea agreement, but then appealed based on the constitutionality of the sex offender registration statute. He contended that certain 1999 and 2005 amendments violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 16. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the amendments at issue did not assign sufficient criminal or penal consequences to transform the statute into a criminal sanction. The registration requirement that appellant was convicted of violating existed in the 1998 version of the sex offender registration statute when appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. Because the various requirements about which appellant complained on appeal were not applied to him, any potential ex post facto effects of those provisions on him were too speculative and attenuated to implicate Tex. Const. art. I, § 16. Moreover, former Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 62.12 required appellant to register for the remainder of his life. The 1999 and 2005 amendments were not properly classified as punitive, even though the failure to register resulted in a criminal penalty.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dallas County Cmty. College Dist. v. Bolton


NO. 02-1110


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


185 S.W.3d 868; 2005 Tex. LEXIS 870; 49 Tex. Sup. J. 180


January 7, 2004, Argued  
December 2, 2005, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Dallas County Cmty. College Dist. v. Bolton, 2006 Tex. LEXIS 130 (Tex., Feb. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FIFTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
Dallas County Comm. College Dist. v. Bolton, 89 S.W.3d 707, 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 7449 (Tex. App. Dallas, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner college district sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals for the Fifth District of Texas, which ordered a reduction in the total amount of recovery, but otherwise affirmed the judgment against the district in respondent students' class action regarding the imposition of fees charged by the district to fund technology purchases and to support student services, claiming that the fees were illegally imposed.


OVERVIEW: The technology and student services fees were changed from flat fees to per-semester-hour fees. The trial court held that the fee was not authorized by law and that the district was required by Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 54.503(f) to obtain student approval for the increase in the student services fee. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, and found that although Tex. Educ. Code Ann. § 130.123(c) specifically authorizes junior colleges to set technology fees and in the language of this section allows junior colleges to pledge the fees to the payment of revenue bonds, it does not restrict the District from charging additional technology fees that are not pledged to revenue bonds. The court also held that the student services fees were voluntarily paid because a waiver was available and no student sought a waiver. Payment of the increased fee was not mandatory; it was contingent on enrollment in a junior college in the district. The class did not establish duress as a matter of law. Therefore, the class was not entitled to a refund of the technology fees or a refund of the increase in the student services fee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals.

Richards v. Tex. A & M Univ. Sys.


No. 10-01-183-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


131 S.W.3d 550; 2004 Tex. App. LEXIS 1424



February 11, 2004, Delivered  
February 11, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by Richards v. Tex. A&M Univ. Sys., 2004 Tex. LEXIS 584 (Tex., June 25, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Richards v. Tex. A&M Univ., 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7733 (U.S., Nov. 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 361st District Court. Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court # 47,822-361.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee filed against appellee former employer under the Anti-Retaliation Law, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. ch. 451 (1996), alleging that he was terminated in retaliation for his workers' compensation claim. The 361st District Court, Brazos County, Texas, granted the employer's motion to dismiss the suit for want of jurisdiction. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the employee's Anti-Retaliation Law suit for want of jurisdiction, finding that the employer, a state university, had sovereign immunity from suit and liability. On the employee's appeal from that decision, the employee claimed that the waiver of sovereign immunity for certain state employees but not for others violated federal and state equal protection rights. The court first determined that the employee had preserved the issue for review under Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a) by raising the equal protection claim in response to the motion to dismiss. However, the court rejected the employee's claim that the Texas Workers' Compensation Act, under which sovereign immunity was not waived for certain governmental employees, violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 3. Immunity was not waived for employes of state institutions that were self-insured for purposes of workers' compensation claims. The court held that the distinction between insured and self-insuring entitles could constitute a valid rational basis for the different treatment regarding sovereign immunity, because insured entities had limited exposure to suits that self-insuring entities lacked.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Saucedo v. State


NO. 03-06-00305-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 4292



May 30, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. D-1-DC-06-904023, HONORABLE MICHAEL LYNCH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District, Texas, which convicted him of third-degree felony driving while intoxicated (DWI), as enhanced by prior convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's vehicle was stopped for erratic driving, and he was charged with DWI. He was later charged by re-indictment with enhanced third-degree felony DWI based upon three prior convictions, two of which occurred in the 1980s. Defendant appealed after he was convicted and the enhancement allegation was found to be true. In affirming, the appellate court noted that former Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701/-1 (repealed by 1993 Tex. Gen. Laws 3586, 3704) contained a time limitation for the use of prior convictions, while Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.09 (2005) did not. The new version of the DWI enhancement law took effect shortly before defendant's conduct in this case. The appellate court rejected defendant's assertion that the 2005 version of the DWI enhancement statute was an ex post facto law under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1 and Tex. Const. art. I, § 16 as applied to him. A legal sufficiency argument was also rejected because former Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.09(e) (repealed by 2005 Tex. Gen. Laws 3363, 3364) did not define an element of the offense. The new version of the law applied since all elements were committed after its enactment date.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Waite v. Waite


NO. 14-00-01330-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


64 S.W.3d 217; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 7795



November 21, 2001, Rendered  
November 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by, 01/31/2002
Motion for rehearing on petition for review denied by, 04/25/2002
Subsequent appeal at Waite v. Waite, 76 S.W.3d 222, 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 3130 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 311th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 99-48049. Warne, Douglas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee wife sought a "no-fault" divorce in the 311th District Court, Harris County, Texas, and appellant husband sought a preliminary injunction to restrain the enforcement of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 6.001 (Vernon 1998). The trial court denied the husband's request, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband's plea to the jurisdiction and declaratory judgment petition argued Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 6.001 (Vernon 1998) involved the trial court in a religious determination of the "legitimate ends of marriage" or the reasonable expectation of "reconciliation." The trial court was only asked to decide if the marriage was intolerable to the other party and of no benefit to society. The legislature could rationally accommodate the termination of a marital relationship without regard to the fault of either partner. This violated neither the Free Exercise or Establishment Clauses of U.S. Const. amend. I nor the "rights of conscience" guarantee of Tex. Const. art. I, § 6. Marriage was not an institution protected by the "free institutions" provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 1. The "open courts" provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, referred to common law causes of action, and not to statutory suits for divorce. The husband's arguments that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 6.502(3), 6.502(7), violated privacy protections of Tex. Const. art. I, § 6, were not ripe. The trial court's interlocutory order awarding the wife attorney fees was not appealable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent patient filed a medical malpractice action against petitioners, hospital and physicians. The trial court granted petitioners' motion for summary judgment, and the Court of Appeals for the Fourth District of Texas reversed. The petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: After experiencing abdominal pain, the patient consulted a doctor in July 2006 and learned that a surgical sponge had been left inside her during a November 1995 hysterectomy. The trial court granted summary judgment, but the court of appeals reversed, holding the statute unconstitutional under the Texas Constitution's Open Courts provision. The reviewing court held that Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.251(b)'s grant of absolute protection against indefinite potential liability did not violate the Texas Constitution.

Post-conviction relief dismissed at Holberg v. State, 2011 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 906 (Tex. Crim. App., Dec. 7, 2011)
Appeal dismissed by Holberg v. State, 2014 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 57 (Tex. Crim. App., Jan. 15, 2014)

PRIOR HISTORY: DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE 251st DISTRICT COURT OF RANDALL COUNTY.
Towery v. Park-Princess, Inc., 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 3571 (Tex. App. Amarillo, May 31, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her capital murder conviction and death sentence in the 251st District Court of Randall county, Texas, contending, in part, that the statutes under which she was convicted and sentenced were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of capital murder and sentenced to death. She appealed directly to the court. Although the court reviewed all 51 points of error raised by appellant, it chose to publish only those issues discussing appellant's contention that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03 and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 37.071 were unconstitutional. The court was not persuaded that the legislative purpose in enacting either statute was to advance or inhibit religion. The primary effect of the statutes was found to be penal in nature, not religious, and the mere fact that the statutes were consistent with the tenets of a particular faith did not render them in violation of the Establishment Clause, U.S. Const. amend. I, or was the court persuaded that the statutes were enacted to advance the Protestant religious belief in "blood atonement". Consistency with the tenets of Protestant faith did not implicate any of the three aspects of the U.S. Const. amend. VIII prohibition on cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court found no reversible error and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Commitment of Fisher


NO. 04-0112


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


164 S.W.3d 637; 2005 Tex. LEXIS 394; 48 Tex. Sup. J. 684


November 30, 2004, Argued  
May 20, 2005, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Fisher v. Tex., 126 S. Ct. 428, 163 L. Ed. 2d 326, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7362 (U.S., Oct. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE THIRTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
Fisher v. State, 123 S.W.3d 828, 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 10697 (Tex. App. Corpus Christi, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State requested review from the Court of Appeal for the Thirteenth District of Texas, which reversed a trial court's determination that respondent suffered from a behavioral abnormality that made him likely to engage in a predatory act of sexual violence and ordered him committed pursuant to the Civil Commitment of Sexually Violent Predators Act (Act), Tex. Health & Safety Code ch. 841.


OVERVIEW: Respondent repeatedly had his parole revoked for committing sexual assault and was adjudicated a sexually violent predator (SVP). The court of appeals held that the Act was punitive, not civil, and violated respondent's due process rights. In analyzing the Kennedy factors, the court held that the Act was civil and therefore due process did not require respondent be competent to stand trial. The court held that while the Act imposed affirmative restraints on respondent, that factor alone did not compel the conclusion that the Act was punitive. No finding of scienter was required to commit an individual found to be an SVP under the Act. Also the Act did not categorically apply only to convicted individuals. The court also found that Act furthered the interests of the state in that the state had authority under its police power to protect the community from the dangerous tendencies of some who were mentally ill. Further, respondent failed to demonstrate that the Act's behavioral abnormality definition was unconstitutionally vague in every application in that the absence of risk levels did not prohibits individualized treatment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals' judgment and rendered the judgment civilly committing respondent to supervision and treatment.

 

157 of 997 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rhine


NO. 2-07-319-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


255 S.W.3d 745; 2008 Tex. App. LEXIS 3221



May 1, 2008, Delivered


NOTICE: PUBLISH.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review granted by State v. Rhine, 2008 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 977 (Tex. Crim. App., Aug. 20, 2008)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Rhine, 2009 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 1307 (Tex. Crim. App., Sept. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
FROM COUNTY CRIMINAL COURT NO. 2 OF DENTON COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violating Tex. Water Code Ann. § 7.177(a)(5) (2000). The State appealed a judgment of the County Criminal Court No. 2 of Denton County, Texas, which granted defendant's motion to quash the information based on the premise that there was an unconstitutional delegation of authority by the legislature to the Texas Commission on Environmental Quality (TCEQ) in violation of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted starting a fire containing crossties, fiberglass, tires, and PVC pipe. The court held that for purposes of the nondelegation doctrine, TCEQ was a public entity. Among other things, TCEQ was subject to the Texas Sunset Act, each of its members was an officer of the State, and the water code did not waive its sovereign immunity from suit. Hence, the heightened scrutiny applied to a private delegation was inapplicable. The nature of the subject of the legislation could not have been practically and efficiently exercised by the legislature because it was neither practical nor efficient for the legislature, which met every other year for a few months, to determine exactly what materials should be banned from outdoor burning, and under what circumstances, including the wind speed, time of day, and other minutiae related to curbing the legislatively-defined "air pollution." The limitations and guidelines of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 382.018 (Supp. 2007) established there was no merit to defendant's claim that the delegation did not contain sufficient guidance concerning what conduct might be prohibited (and made a criminal offense) under the power delegated.


OUTCOME: The case was reversed and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Fort Bend County Wrecker Ass'n v. Wright


NO. 01-99-00431-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


39 S.W.3d 421; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 1120



February 22, 2001, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 268th District Court. Trial Court Cause No. 105844. Fort Bend County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wrecker association applied for a permanent injunction to restrain the appellee sheriff department from enforcing wrecker rules. A hearing for a permanent injunction was held by 268th District Court (Texas). The trial court permanently enjoined the appellee from enforcing the provision of the wrecker rules that a price cap. All other relief was denied. Appellant challenged the trial court's decision. Appellee cross appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellee sheriff department maintained a list of wrecker and towing companies. Appellee used this list to determine which towing company would be assigned to tow cars when appellee requested a non-consensual tow. Appellee enacted numerous rules and regulations specifying the requirements that wrecker truck companies had to meet in order to stay on appellee's list. Among those rules was a price cap of $ 75. The legitimacy of the rules was the subject of this appeal. The appellate court did not find the appellee's wrecker policy to be an ordinance violating the separation of powers doctrine. By definition, a departmental policy designed to refer business to a particular set of tow companies was not a law, regulation, or a provision having the force and effect of law. Appellee was allowed to create a wrecker rotation list and maintain policies in accordance with the list. The record revealed the trial judge granted a permanent injunction as to appellee's price caps because he was concerned the appellee was not in compliance with a Texas Attorney General Opinion. The opinion was not applicable to the case.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of the permanent injunction as to the appellee's price caps was not supported by probative evidence and constituted an abuse of discretion. In all other respects, the order of the trial court was affirmed. Appellee's wrecker policy did not constitute an ordinance, law or regulation. Appellee could create a wrecker rotation list.
