160 of 997 DOCUMENTS



Garza v. Zachry Constr. Corp.


No. 04-11-00101-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


373 S.W.3d 715; 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 4064



May 23, 2012, Delivered 
May 23, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for review denied by Garza v. Zachry Constr. Corp., 2012 Tex. LEXIS 872 (Tex., Oct. 12, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
From the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 2008-CI-12469. Honorable Fred Shannon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party challenged a decision from the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, which entered a take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellees, a subcontractor and its two employees, in an action alleging negligence and respondeat superior.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was working in a plant alongside the subcontractor's employees. After an accident, the injured party sued the subcontractor and its employees. The trial court rendered a take-nothing summary judgment in favor of the subcontractor and its two employees. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that recovery of workers' compensation benefits was an exclusive remedy under Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 408.001(a) (2006). The immunity of a general contractor extended to subcontractors where the general contractor had purchased workers' compensation insurance that covered all of the workers on the site, pursuant to Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 406.123(a). Under its contract with the subcontractor, the general contractor agreed to provide workers' compensation insurance to the subcontractor, thereby creating the legal fiction of the general contractor as the "deemed employer" and the subcontractor and its employees as "deemed employees." Next, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 406.123, 408.001 were not unconstitutional under Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The restriction on the right to bring common law tort claims was not unreasonable or arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gard v. Bandera County Appraisal Dist.


No. 04-08-00802-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


293 S.W.3d 613; 2009 Tex. App. LEXIS 3048



May 6, 2009, Delivered 
May 6, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
From the 216th Judicial District Court, Bandera County, Texas Trial Court No. 8494-02. Honorable Stephen B. Ables, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed suit against defendant county review board in the 216th Judicial District Court, Bandera County, Texas, challenging the appraised values of his property. A mediation agreement resolved all issues relating to the appraised values, but the parties agreed to submit the issue of attorney's fees to the trial court for determination. The trial court awarded the taxpayer $ 700 in attorney's fees, and the taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that the upper and lower ceilings on recoverable attorney's fees in Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.29 (2008) was a violation of substantive due process. The court rejected this premise. The protected property right could not be the right to recover attorney's fees, because fees were recoverable only under a contract or by statute. Rather, the taxpayer argued that the cap deprived taxpayers of a due process right to obtain legal representation. However, the taxpayer failed to show that a taxpayer could not obtain counsel and failed to prove that the challenged governmental action was not rationally related to furthering a legitimate state interest. With regard to the law's alleged interference with the constitutional right of access to the courts, the taxpayer made no showing that such was the case. Moreover, civil litigants were not required to be represented by counsel and thousands of cases each year were prosecuted by pro se litigants. Although the court rejected the taxpayer's claim, it held that his appeal was not objectively frivolous.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, and the county board's request for sanctions was denied.

Ex parte Buchhorn


No. 04-00-00606-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 2479



April 18, 2001, Delivered  
April 18, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the County Court at Law No. 8, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. No. 750432. Honorable Karen Crouch, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 8, Bexar County, Texas, denying his application for writ of habeas corpus in which he had challenged the constitutionality of the statute prohibiting indecent exposure as unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged by information and complaint with the offense of indecent exposure. He challenged the constitutionality of the statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.08, prohibiting indecent exposure as unconstitutionally vague through a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court denied appellant's application. On appeal, the appellant argued that because the Texas Penal Code did not define the terms "offended" or "alarmed," § 21.08 was unconstitutionally vague. Judgment was affirmed. The court concluded that a statute was not rendered unconstitutionally vague merely because all words or terms were not specifically defined. It found the terms "offended" and "alarmed" were words with meanings well known by people of ordinary intelligence. Finding that exposing one's anus or genitals with the intent to arouse or gratify one's sexual desire was, by its very nature, often calculated to alarm or offend, the court held that § 21.08 gave fair notice of the prohibition against the proscribed conduct.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; the applicable penal statute prohibiting indecent public exposure was not unconstitutionally vague, as the statute gave people of ordinary intelligence fair notice that such conduct was forbidden, regardless of its lack of definitions for the terms "alarmed" or "offended."

167 of 997 DOCUMENTS



Ward County Irrigation Dist. No. 1 v. Red Bluff Water Power Control Dist.


No. 08-04-00322-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


170 S.W.3d 696; 2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 5063



June 30, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 26, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 143rd District Court of Ward County, Texas. (TC# 04-05-20749-CVW).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant irrigation and water improvement districts challenged a decision from the 143rd District Court of Ward County (Texas), which determined that the irrigation districts were no longer members of appellee water power control district after their conversion from water improvement districts.


OVERVIEW: The power control district refused to seat directors from the irrigation districts on the board of directors due to a conversion from a water improvement district. The power control district filed a declaratory judgment action to settle the dispute. After the trial court entered judgment in favor of the power control district, the irrigation districts and a water improvement district sought review. In reversing, the court determined that a restrictive approach to former Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7807d and Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 7807dd (now codified in Tex. Water Code Ann. ch. 51) was inconsistent with the Texas Legislature's intent regarding the conversion of one type of water district to another. The Legislature did not intend to restrict membership in water power control districts to water improvement districts; rather, it intended only to exclude the more powerful water control and improvement districts. Moreover, there was no meaningful difference in powers after the conversion to irrigation districts took place under Tex. Water Code Ann. §§ 58.122, 58.042. The court rejected the argument that membership was not allowed due to different election procedures.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and a declaratory judgment was entered in favor of the irrigation and water improvement districts.

In re D.L.C.


NO. 2-02-163-CV, NO. 2-02-164-CV, NO. 2-02-170-CV, NOS. 2-02-171-CV, 2-02-172-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


124 S.W.3d 354; 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 10619



December 18, 2003, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF DENTON COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juveniles were adjudicated in the County Court at Law No. 1 of Denton County (Texas) for indecency with a child, aggravated sexual assault of a child, or both. Each juvenile was required to register in the sex offender registration program. After the Texas DNA statute, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.0405 (2002), was passed, the trial court amended each juveniles' probation to require him to submit a DNA specimen. The juveniles appealed.


OVERVIEW: The juveniles contended that requiring them to submit a DNA sample was unconstitutional and that the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support the trial court's finding that they should be subject to the DNA statute. On appeal, the court found that (1) the DNA statute did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause; (2) the juveniles failed to demonstrate that, as applied to them, the Texas DNA statute violated the Double Jeopardy Clause; (3) the search and seizure occasioned by the DNA statute did not violate the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution; (4) the Texas DNA statute did not violate the Self-Incrimination Clause; (5) because the juveniles were adjudicated of a qualifying offense and were placed on probation, the prerequisites for applying the DNA statute were met; (6) there was evidence of probative force supporting the trial court's amendment of the juveniles' probation conditions to add the requirement that they provide a DNA specimen; and (7) the trial court's amendment of the probation conditions was not so against the great weight and preponderance of the evidence as to be manifestly unjust.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Zaragosa v. Chemetron Invs., Inc.


NO. 2-00-328-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


122 S.W.3d 341; 2003 Tex. App. LEXIS 9480; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,814



November 6, 2003, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 236TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured individual challenged a decision of the 236th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee companies in connection with the individual's products liability action alleging strict liability, breach of express and implied warranty, and negligence.


OVERVIEW: While working near an opening of a large, commercial mixer/blender, the individual claimed that his right hand got caught in the equipment, which resulted in a partial amputation. He filed this products liability action, but the trial court granted the companies summary judgment. The court affirmed on appeal. By using the ordinary meaning of the phrase "tangible personal property" provided by the legislature and the state supreme court, the textured vegetable protein manufactured and processed by the mixer/blender clearly fell within the meaning of the term, and thus the mixer/blender was the type of manufacturing equipment governed by the statute of repose in Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.012 and no genuine issue of fact existed on this issue. The statute of repose barred the individual's lawsuit under § 16.012 because it was conclusively shown that the mixer/blender was sold more than 15 years before the date the individual filed the action. The court rejected the individual's attack on the constitutionality of the statute. It was reasonably related to the legitimate state purpose of protecting manufacturers and sellers from stale claims based on manufacturing equipment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Holmes v. Beatty


NO. 07-0784 - consolidated with - NO. 07-0785


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


290 S.W.3d 852; 2009 Tex. LEXIS 462; 52 Tex. Sup. J. 967


December 5, 2008, Argued 
June 26, 2009, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Holmes v. Beatty, 2009 Tex. LEXIS 1124 (Tex., Sept. 25, 2009)
Rehearing denied by Holmes v. Beatty, 2009 Tex. LEXIS 1123 (Tex., Sept. 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FOURTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS. ON PETITION FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE FOURTEENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.
Beatty v. Holmes, 233 S.W.3d 475, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 6420 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., 2007)
Holmes v. Beatty, 233 S.W.3d 494, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 6421 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., 2007)



DISPOSITION:  The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed and rendered as to the designation of two accounts and affirmed as to the designation of one account; the judgment was reversed as to the designation of the securities certificates.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Texas trial court found that some of the decedents' assets were held jointly with survivorship rights and others were community property. The Court of Appeals for the Fourteenth District of Texas affirmed in part, reversed and rendered in part, and remanded for further proceedings. Respondent, executor of the wife's estate, and petitioner, son of the husband's estate, petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that a "joint tenancy" or "JT TEN" designation on an account was sufficient to create rights of survivorship in community property under Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 452. Two of the decedents' accounts included this designation, which was sufficient to indicate their intent to hold those accounts with rights of survivorship. As to another account, the designation "Joint (WROS)" meant joint tenancy with rights of survivorship. This indicated the decedents' intent to obtain rights of survivorship in this account. Because the agreements' survivorship language conferred survivorship rights in the securities certificates until the decedents' deposed of them, the certificates passed to the husband pursuant to those rights. By enacting Tex. Prob. Code Ann. § 46(b) at the same time as sections 451 through 462 (Chapter XI, Part 3 of the Probate Code), the Legislature provided that Part 3 was the exclusive means to establish rights of survivorship in community property. The certificates issues from certain accounts retained survivorship rights established by those accounts' agreements. The agreement to another account established rights of survivorship in the account.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed and rendered as to the designation of two accounts and affirmed as to the designation of one account; the judgment was reversed as to the designation of the securities certificates.

Black v. State


NO. 73,197


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TEXAS


26 S.W.3d 895; 2000 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 78



September 13, 2000, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM BELL COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(h), appellant filed automatic direct appeal from sentence of death upon his conviction for child capital murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(8), in the District Court of Bell County (Texas), claiming that the statute violated the Equal Protection Clauses of both U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 3.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of child capital murder, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(8). Pursuant to the jury's answers, the trial judge sentenced the appellant to death. Under the automatic direct appeal provisions of the death penalty statute, Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 37.071, § 2(h), the court affirmed, holding that the child capital-murder provision was rationally related to the government's interest in protecting young children, and thus, did not violate Equal Protection Clauses of either the U.S. Const. amend. XIV or the Tex. Const. art. I, § 3. Further, designating the victim's status as a young child was an aggravating element that did not require proof of an offender's specific intent as to an appellant's knowledge of the child's age, only proof that the child was under six. The court further held that the trial judge properly exercised his discretion in excusing a prospective juror who had a hearing impairment and the appellant's presence would not have changed the court's ability to make such a decision.


OUTCOME: Conviction and death penalty was affirmed; child capital-murder provision was rationally related to compelling government interest, and thus, did not violate equal protection. Designating victim's status as a young child was an aggravating element that did not require proof of specific intent of age. Trial judge properly exercised discretion in excusing prospective juror outside appellant's presence.

February 8, 2000, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court of Appeals. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MC98-R0059-D, MC98-R0060-D, MC98-R0061-D.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgments of the County Criminal Court of Appeals, Dallas County, Texas, affirming her convictions for operating a motor vehicle with expired vehicle registration and inspection stickers and without a driver's license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of traffic offenses in a trial before a municipal court of record, and the county criminal court of appeals affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellant argued that the municipal judge was the injured party in her cases and should have been disqualified. Appellant was accused, however, of traffic offenses in which there was no injured party. The appellate provisions of the former Garland Municipal Court of Record Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §30.00910 (repealed; recodified at Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 30.00027(b) (Supp. 2000)) (Act), were not so complex as to deprive her of due process. The Act was not a local or special law prohibited by Tex. Const. art. III, § 56, because the authority to pass a statute establishing courts in a particular city was given under Tex. Const. art. V, § 1. The assistant city attorney was allowed to represent the State.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed; municipal judge was not injured party in appellant's traffic offenses; applicable appellate rules were not so complex as to deprive appellant of due process; legislature was empowered to enact a statute establishing courts in a particular city, and the State could be represented by an assistant city attorney.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 4, Bexar County (Texas), which denied his application for writ of habeas corpus in an indecent exposure case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged by information with committing the offense of indecent exposure, which was prohibited by Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.08 (1994). Appellant challenged the constitutionality of § 21.08 by application for writ of habeas corpus, and the trial court denied the application. He appealed, arguing that § 21.08 was unconstitutionally vague because it did not define the term "offended" and "alarmed." The court reasoned that while an actor may be unaware that some acts may alarm or offend another person, exposing one's anus or genitals with the intent to arouse or gratify a person's sexual desire is not the type of conduct that leaves an actor unaware that such conduct might be alarming or offensive.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed the denial of appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus, because indecent exposure statute was not unconstitutionally vague as the words "offended" and "alarmed" were terms with meanings that were well-known by people of ordinary intelligence.

Gilmore v. State


No. 11-96-00383-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


2005 Tex. App. LEXIS 5220



July 7, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] PLEASE CONSULT THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Taylor County.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a trial court which found him guilty of aggravated assault and sentenced him to confinement for 20 years. Upon original submission, the court held that defendant was harmed because the jury was not allowed to consider the lesser included offense. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Texas) reversed and remanded the cause for consideration of defendant's remaining three points of error.


OVERVIEW: After the jury retired to deliberate, it sent a note to the trial court, asking whether defendant would get credit for time served and, if so, how long had he been in jail. The trial court answered that defendant would get credit for the time he had been in jail and advised the jury to recall the evidence on the length of time he had been in jail. The court held that the additional instruction was proper because it did not pertain to factual matters and was a correct statement of law under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.03, § 2(a) (Supp. 2004-2005). Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a) specifically authorized the enactment of legislation permitting courts to inform juries about the effect of good conduct time and eligibility for parole on the period of incarceration served by the defendant. In addition, there was no infringement by the trial court on the clemency powers of the executive. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in concluding that a juror could not perform her duties as a juror, dismissing her on the second day of trial, and proceeding with only 11 jurors where the juror had a sick child with no one to help take care of him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Perry v. Del Rio


NO. 01-0988 - consolidated with - NO. 01-1002


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


67 S.W.3d 85; 2001 Tex. LEXIS 98; 45 Tex. Sup. J. 52


October 18, 2001, Argued  
October 19, 2001, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON DIRECT APPEALS FOR THE 353RD DISTRICT COURT, TRAVIS COUNTY, TEXAS.

Perry v. Del Rio, 66 S.W.3d 239, 2001 Tex. LEXIS 81, 44 Tex. Sup. Ct. J. 1147 (Tex. 2001) 



DISPOSITION: Trial Court violated Due Course of Law provision of Texas Constitution, Judgment of Trial Court Vacated, Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee individuals in the 353rd District Court, Travis County (Texas), challenged the constitutionality of the existing state congressional districts and asked the court to adopt a new redistricting plan. The trial court enjoined the parties from using the existing districts and adopted a new redistricting plan. Appellant state officials and others appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Texas Attorney General proposed a redistricting plan as the base plan for federal redistricting. The trial court refused to accept the plan, used a state legislative council for expert assistance in developing a plan, and required the council to keep the communications between the trial court and the council confidential. The trial court accepted for review comments and suggestions from the parties. The trial court then modified its plan, based on a recommendation of another party, and ordered its plan into enactment without giving the parties the opportunity to review or comment on the plan. On appeal, the supreme court found the attorney general, under the separation-of-powers doctrine, did not have the authority to require the trial court to adopt his redistricting plan and render judgment that his plan was the baseline state court plan for the redistricting proceedings. Additionally, the trial court violated the parties' due process rights when it rendered a judgment based on the new plans not in evidence at trial without giving the parties an opportunity for a meaningful hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Ex parte Barnett


No. 10-13-00339-CR

182 of 997 DOCUMENTS



McCullough v. Godwin


NO. 12-05-00422-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


214 S.W.3d 793; 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 978



February 9, 2007, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 9, 2007.
Rehearing denied by McCullough v. Godwin, 2007 Tex. App. LEXIS 2077 (Tex. App. Tyler, Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HENDERSON COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment from the Third Judicial District Court of Henderson County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, the father of a deceased child and two of the father's friends, in the mother's action alleging wrongful death, survival, negligence, and gross negligence.


OVERVIEW: The father and two of his friends took the child swimming at a lake, and the child drowned. The court held that the father was entitled to summary judgment under the parental immunity doctrine. Although the mother presented evidence that the father was intoxicated and that he did not supervise the child adequately, such actions did not amount to abandonment and abdication of parental responsibility. The mother's failure to make citations to the record regarding an allegation of malice waived that issue under Tex. R. App. P. 38.1(h). The trial court erred in granting summary judgment to the friends on the ground that they had no duty of supervision because their pleadings failed to rebut other alleged duties; however, the error did not require reversal. There was no evidence that the friends committed a wrongful act within the meaning of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 71.002, 71.021 or acted with gross negligence under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 41.001(11); a reasonable person would not foresee that a child would drown while his father, who had a duty of care with regard to that child under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 14.001(a)(2) (Supp. 2006), was present.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


 

183 of 997 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of R.M.H.


No. 04-11-00095-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 6009



August 3, 2011, Delivered 
August 3, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by In the Interest of R.M.H., 2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 9241 (Tex. App. San Antonio, Aug. 24, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
From the 216th Judicial District Court, Bandera County, Texas. Trial Court No. FL-09-441. The Honorable Cathy O. Morris, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a father and a mother, challenged a decision of the 216th Judicial District Court, Bandera County (Texas), which, on a petition filed by appellee Texas Department of Family and Protective Services, terminated their parental rights to their child under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 161.001(1)(D), (E) (Supp. 2010) and found that their statement of points under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 263.405(b) (2008) was frivolous.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother raised certain issues, but the court affirmed. The statements of appellate points filed by a father and mother contained specific challenges to the sufficiency of the evidence and were sufficient to preserve the issues for review. Given that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 263.405(i) (2008) did not preclude the father or mother from raising their sufficiency of the evidence issues, their challenges based on due process and equal protection failed. The mother and father did not allege there were any meritorious issues they were precluded from raising on appeal because of the application of § 263.405(i). Thus, they failed to show that the statute was unconstitutionally applied to them. They claimed that a competent appellate attorney could only determine whether there were arguable points after a careful review of the record, but the court previously held this argument insufficient to show facial unconstitutionality of § 263.405(i). The mother and father did not argue why the record made at the hearing on a motion for a new trial would be insufficient, and the court declined to order a full record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

184 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Cole


NO. 2-00-226-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


43 S.W.3d 713; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 2407



April 12, 2001, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the 297th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas ) of two counts of aggravated assault on a public servant with a deadly weapon. The trial court denied defendant's motion to reinstate bond pending appeal. The trial court then denied defendant's application for writ of habeas corpus. Defendant appealed the denial of his post-conviction application for writ of habeas corpus seeking bond pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's convictions, a surety posted bond pending appeal for defendant. When defendant was arrested on another crime to be held without bond, the trial court denied bond pending appeal to defendant. The defendant argued the trial court erred by retroactively applying Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.04(b), as amended effective September 1, 1999, to his cases already on appeal at the time and by failing to reinstate his bonds. The appellate court found the trial court did not err in its decision. Application of art. 44.04(b), as amended, was not prohibited by the Ex Post Facto Clause of the constitution. Further, defendant was not constitutionally guaranteed the right to bail pending appeal. Therefore, amended art. 44.04(b) did not violate the prohibition against retroactive laws under the Texas Constitution. Moreover, amended art. 44.04(b) was applied only after the effective date of the amendment. Finally, under either version of art. 44.04, the trial court could deny bail pending appeal if it appeared likely that the defendant would commit another offense while on bail.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed.

Dep't of Protective v. Schutz


NO. 01-00-01245-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


101 S.W.3d 512; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 9015



December 19, 2002, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [**1] PUBLISH. TEX. R. APP. P. 47.4.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 306th District Court. Galveston County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 00-CV-0194.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, foster parents, sought a declaratory judgment in the 306th District Court, Galveston County (Texas) from the Department of Protective and Regulatory Services (the department) that the definition of "neglect" in Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 261.001(4)(B)(i) (Vernon 2002) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the foster mother and that she was not guilty of neglect. The department appealed the trial court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: A 14-month-old foster child who lived with the foster parents drowned in their backyard swimming pool. The department argued that Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. § 42 applied. The foster parents argued Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 261 applied. The appeals court held that because they operated a foster home within the meaning of Tex. Hum. Res. Code Ann. § 261.309(e), the foster parents did not have the right to file suit in the district court without submitting to a formal administrative hearing. They were required to submit to an administrative hearing regardless of whether the Human Resources Code or the Family Code applied. Because the foster mother had not exhausted her administrative remedies, the district court did not have subject-matter jurisdiction over her due-process claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was dismissed.

 

186 of 997 DOCUMENTS


Hebert v. Hopkins


NO. 03-11-00419-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


395 S.W.3d 884; 2013 Tex. App. LEXIS 2100



March 1, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TOM GREEN COUNTY, 391ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. D-10-0285-C, HONORABLE THOMAS J. GOSSETT, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and his wife, brought a health care liability claim against appellees, a doctor and his practice, in the District Court of Tom Green County, 391st Judicial District (Texas). The trial court dismissed the case for failure to serve an adequate expert report required by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. ch. 74, either originally or as supplemented, and appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants said it was an abuse of discretion to dismiss their suit. The appellate court held it was no abuse of discretion to find an expert's reports gave insufficient information on standard of care and breach to find if their claims had merit, as required by Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 74.351(r)(6) (2011), because a trial court could find the expert (1) recognized an exception to criticisms of a doctor's treatment, (2) did not state when the exception applied, (3) did not state if the patient presented such a situation, and (4) begged the question as to whether the doctor's precautions met the standard of care. A supplemental report did not cure the deficiencies because it did not address deficiencies as to the standard of care and breach. Appellants did not show the expert-report requirement was unconstitutional because they did not show (1) lack of a rational basis for distinguishing between health care liability claimants and other litigants, (2) it interfered with the judiciary by barring their suit, as opposed to the lack of an adequate report, (3) it arbitrarily violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 13 by requiring an expert report sooner rather than later.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Union Carbide Corp. v. Synatzske


NO. 01-09-0114 1-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


2011 Tex. App. LEXIS 4934



June 30, 2011, Opinion Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, On reconsideration by, En banc Union Carbide Corp. v. Synatzske, 2012 Tex. App. LEXIS 5187 (Tex. App. Houston 1st Dist., June 28, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
On Appeal from the 11th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 2007-43950.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order of the 11th District Court, Harris County, Texas, denying its motion to dismiss a wrongful death action filed by appellees, representatives and co-executrixes of the employee's estate.


OVERVIEW: Appellees alleged that the employee's death was caused by his exposure to asbestos when he worked for the employer. On appeal, the court held that appellees' expert report did not comply with Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 90.010(f)(1)(B)(ii) (2011) because the pulmonary function testing performed on the employee by the employer 40 years before the employee's death and provided no evidence of impairment could not be used to satisfy the pulmonary function testing requirement. However, the court held that § 90.010(f)(1)(B)(ii)'s requirement of a verification that the employee had had a pulmonary function testing performed on him in order for appellees to assert their asbestos-related claims was unconstitutional as applied to them under Tex. Const. art. I, § 16 because it was undisputed that at the time of the employee's death, a physician report containing a pulmonary function test was not required, such a test could not be performed on the employee before he died, and the evidence on file showed that appellees' claims had a substantial basis in fact. In addition, no public interest would be served by § 90.010(f)(1)(B)(ii)'s application to appellees.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Garcia v. State


NUMBER 13-00-298-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 7370



November 1, 2001, Delivered  
November 1, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 156th District Court of Bee County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault and was placed on deferred probation by the 156th District Court of Bee County (Texas). Subsequently, his probation was revoked and he was sentenced to 11 years' confinement. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's appeal contained three points of error: he should not be barred from appealing the revocation of his deferred adjudication probation, because if Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b), precluded appellate review of deferred adjudication revocation probation hearings, it violated the equal protection clauses of the United States and Texas Constitutions; Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b), was unconstitutional because it divested the Texas Court of Appeals of their appellate jurisdiction to entertain criminal appeals, in violation of the Texas Constitution; and the trial court abused its discretion in revoking his probation. The law did not provide appellate review from a decision to adjudicate guilt in a deferred adjudication proceeding, and because the right to appeal was not a constitutional right, not providing such right in deferred adjudication proceeding was not unconstitutional. There was a rational basis for treating adjudication probationers differently from regular probationers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hancock


No. 10-99-290-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


35 S.W.3d 199; 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 8305



December 13, 2000, Delivered  
December 13, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the County Court at Law No. 1 McLennan County, Texas. Trial Court # 984575 CR1.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the County Court at Law, McLennan County, Texas, dismissing the information charging defendant with the offense of keeping a gambling place on grounds that the controlling statutes, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.01(4) (Supp. 2001) and Tex. Penal Code § 47.04 (1994), were unconstitutionally vague to give him notice of the prohibited conduct.


OVERVIEW: The information alleged that defendant used a building as a gambling place, namely, a place used for playing eight-liners and slot machines, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.04(a) (1994). At a pretrial hearing, defendant argued that because the information charged that his "gambling place" was "a place used for playing eight-liners and slot machines," the State necessarily had to prove that eight-liners and slot machines were gambling devices. However, according to defendant, Tex. Penal Code 47.01(4)(B) (Supp. 2001), which defined a gambling device, was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him. The trial court agreed. The State appealed. Following the reasoning of a recent case of the Texas Third Court of Appeals, the appellate court held that the trial court erred when it found § 47.01(4)(B) to be unconstitutionally vague as applied to the prosecution of eight-liners. It reversed the order dismissing the information and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order dismissing the information was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The portion of the Texas Penal Code defining "gambling device" was not unconstitutionally vague as it applied to the prosecution of eight-liners.

Rogers v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 188th Judicial District Court. Gregg County, Texas. Trial Court No. 26968-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the 188th Judicial District Court, Gregg County, Texas, of aggravated assault, and was sentenced to 60 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of shooting his former girlfriend. The jury in defendant's first trial imposed a life sentence. The sentence was reversed on appeal, because the trial court failed to give the mandatory instruction required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4 (Vernon Supp. 2002) and gave an incomplete response to the jury's question as to the length of time defendant would actually have to serve before being eligible for release. Defendant argued that the trial court erred at resentencing by giving a version of the instruction that varied from the language of the statute and that giving the instruction deprived defendant of due process. The appellate court held that the differences in the charge given were insignificant and did not harm defendant. Defendant's due process contention that it was error to give the charge when defendant was not eligible for good time credit had previously been rejected by the court. The instruction, as given, substantially complied with the requirements of the statute. Further, defendant's argument to the jury invited any error that may have occurred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lawrence v. CDB Servs.


NO. 00-0142, NO. 00-0201


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


44 S.W.3d 544; 2001 Tex. LEXIS 21; 44 Tex. Sup. J. 554


October 2, 2000, Argued  
March 29, 2001, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON PETITIONS FOR REVIEW FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE SEVENTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In petitioner employees' consolidated actions to recover damages for injuries sustained on the job, the Court of Appeals for the Seventh District of Texas granted respondent employers summary judgment based upon petitioners' prior waiver of any such claims. Petitioners challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, who were nonsubscribers to workers' compensation insurance, employed petitioners. Petitioners voluntarily elected to participate in employer benefit plans that provided injured employees specified benefits in lieu of common-law remedies. Petitioners sued respondents after they were injured at work. The trial court granted respondents summary judgment based upon petitioners' election in the employer benefit plans. On appeal, the supreme court affirmed. The Texas Workers' Compensation Act did not expressly prohibit the elections petitioners signed, and therefore they were enforceable. Absent clear legislative intent to prohibit such agreements, the court held that the agreements between petitioners and respondents were not void on public policy grounds, and that any public policy concerns should be addressed by the state legislature. The court also held that the waiver one petitioner signed satisfied the fair-notice and express-negligence tests.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the Texas Workers' Compensation Act did not expressly prohibit petitioners from voluntarily electing to participate in respondents' employee benefits plans in lieu of exercising common-law remedies.

Brenneman v. State


NUMBER 13-99-235-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


45 S.W.3d 729; 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 2278



April 5, 2001, Delivered  
April 5, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for discretionary review refused by, 08/29/2001


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the hate crimes enhancement of his sentence entered by the 228th District Court of Harris County, Texas, for assault, contending that Tex. Code of Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.014 (Vernon Supp. 2001) of the Texas Hate Crime Statute, under which the judge found that appellant selected his victim primarily because of his bias or prejudice against homosexuals, was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that he was walking his dog in the vicinity of a gay bar one evening, when appellant called him a "pervert" and a "homosexual", before attacking him with a knife. Appellant was charged with aggravated assault, under an indictment which included a hate crimes enhancement paragraph. The jury found him guilty of the lesser-included offense of assault. At the punishment phase, appellant urged a motion to quash the indictment on grounds that the Texas Hate Crimes Statute was void for vagueness in violation of the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The trial court denied the motion and entered a finding that appellant selected the victim primarily because of appellant's bias and prejudice against homosexuals. The appellate court interpreted appellant's brief as conceding that the statute as applied to him involved a legitimate and specific bias group, homosexuals. By failing to first establish that Tex. Code of Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.014 (Vernon Supp. 2001) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him, appellant waived his challenge to the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Gonzales v. Brazos River Harbor Navigation Dist.


NO. 14-99-00272 -CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 5702



August 24, 2000, Rendered

195 of 997 DOCUMENTS


In re Allcat Claims Serv., L.P.


NO. 11-0589


SUPREME COURT OF TEXAS


356 S.W.3d 455; 2011 Tex. LEXIS 896; 55 Tex. Sup. J. 103


October 24, 2011, Argued 
November 28, 2011, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 13, 2012.
As Corrected January 27, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY: Allcat Claims Serv., L.P. v. Combs, 2011 Tex. LEXIS 808 (Tex., Oct. 21, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On petition for writ of mandamus, relators, a partnership and a limited partner, sought an order directing respondents, the Comptroller and Attorney General, to refund franchise taxes paid under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.001, a declaration that the franchise tax was unconstitutional under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 24, in a facial and as-applied challenge, and an award of attorney fees under the Declaratory Judgments Act.


OVERVIEW: Relators argued that the franchise tax, Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.001, violated Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 24. The court held that the tax did not facially violate the constitution, and the court lacked jurisdiction to consider the as applied challenge and the fee award issue. The court held that Act of May 2, 2006, 79th Leg., 3d C.S., ch. 1, § 24, 2006 Tex. Gen. Laws 1, 1-41, served as a specific, limited exception to the generalized provisions of the Tax Code that conferred exclusive jurisdiction over certain suits on the district courts of Travis County, like relators' suit in this case. The court had jurisdiction under Tex. Const. art. V, § 3(a) and case law did not stand as impediments to that jurisdiction. Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 24 did not preclude the taxation of business entities for the privilege of doing business in Texas and taking advantage of the option to limit the liability of business owners via a limited partnership structure. The franchise tax did not constitute a tax on the net income of relators' natural-person limited partners within the meaning of the Article VIII, § 24, and relators' facial challenge lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court denied the mandamus requests relating to the partnership's facial challenge. The court dismissed the as-applied challenge and the attorney fee claim for lack of jurisdiction.

In re M.P.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 386th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), denied defendant juvenile's motion to quash, challenging the constitutionality of former Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.014 and former Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.47, and found that he had engaged in delinquent conduct, specifically graffiti. Also, the trial court found that he had selected the victim on the basis of race and sentenced him to the Texas Youth Commission. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of engaging in delinquent conduct, specifically graffiti. Defendant was sentenced to the Texas Youth Commission until his 21st birthday. On appeal, defendant challenged the trial court's sentencing order, claiming that his due process rights were violated and reasserting his position that former Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Thus, defendant failed to meet his burden with regard to the facial challenge that the statutes were unconstitutional and the appellate court overruled his sole issue on appeal.

Williams v. Razor Enters.


No. 04-01-00134-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


70 S.W.3d 274; 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 96



January 9, 2002, Delivered  
January 9, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 288th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 1997-CI-17967. Honorable Janet P. Littlejohn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee filed a workers' compensation claim after suffering a work-related injury. The 288th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee challenged the constitutionality of the exclusive remedy provision of the Texas Workers' Compensation Act, specifically, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 406.123 and 406.144, claiming that those provisions violated the open courts guarantee of the Texas Constitution. The appeals court disagreed. The employee argued that these provisions violated the open courts guarantee because they permitted a general contractor, such as the employer, to benefit from workers' compensation coverage while passing the costs of that coverage down to a laborer, such as the employee. This stance entirely missed the point of the law. As an employee, he benefitted from a limited, but guaranteed right to workers' compensation benefits, and this benefit served as an adequate substitute to his common law claim, wherein recovery was conditioned upon his ability to prove his employer's negligence. So long as there was a compensation policy in force, the manner in which the insurance was paid was immaterial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Martinez v. State


No. 08-12-00320-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


503 S.W.3d 728; 2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 12281



November 16, 2016, Decided


NOTICE: PUBLISH


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 41st District Court of El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 20120D02642).
Martinez v. State, 2014 Tex. App. LEXIS 13666 (Tex. App. El Paso, Dec. 19, 2014)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Texas Legislature did not violate the separation of powers provision and acted within its constitutional powers in directing that the 2015 amendment to Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 841.085 be applied retroactively to cases pending on appeal because the Legislature did not usurp or unduly interfere with the clemency power of the executive branch; the Legislature did not violate the separation of powers provision in the Texas Constitution, when it directed that the amendments decriminalizing defendant's conduct be applied retroactively to defendant's case even though it was pending on appeal.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed and judgment rendered dismissing indictment.

Siller v. State


No. 11-15-00016-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


2016 Tex. App. LEXIS 8733



August 11, 2016, Decided 
August 11, 2016, Opinion Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISH. TEX. R. APP. 47.2


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, in part, Remanded by, Petition for discretionary review granted by Siller v. State, 2017 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 703 (Tex. Crim. App., Oct. 4, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] On Appeal from the 42nd District Court, Taylor County, Texas. Trial Court Cause. No. 25561A.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The search warrant at issue in this case was not supported by probable cause; [2]-The search warrant in this case was not supported by probable cause because the Penal Code section upon which it was based was later declared to be unconstitutional; [3]-The absence of probable cause to support the search warrant precluded the application of the good faith exception contained in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23(b).


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.
